O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, my very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last part of the science of medicine together with its fulfillment and have made the end through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would accomplish it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is treated in our region and is foreign throughout, so the science is lost and decayed, and nothing remains of the virtues except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and knowledge is driven away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I will revive it together with the order of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation. 
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And I will bring together the forms of the cautery irons and the other instruments of the work with the fitting of their declaration and preparation, as it is necessary. 
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for whoever undertakes this to be learned in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the placement of the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of arteries, and the movement and rest of the veins, and their place of origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this reason Hippocrates says that knowledge without practice is nothing, and with practice it is something. 
et meismement en l’art de main.	and the same in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We say at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned will beware lest he fall into error and harm people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Just as I have seen many times more than those who interfere with this science and abandon their knowledge and experience. 
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish barber who lanced an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries in her neck. 
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Because so much blood flowed out that the woman died between his hands.  
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another barber who treated a stone of an old man, and the stone was large; 
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	He took out with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.  
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew that if it were cut out he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another barber who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break he had a wound; 
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the barber, full of ignorance, removed the break above the wound with sharp tools, and did not leave the wound any dressing, and left it like that until the end.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	And he commanded him not to unbind it; 
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and let it stay like that until the leg was all swollen and the foot, and came to ruin. 
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come untie the leg;  
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I untied it, it was so easy and he did not feel any pain. 
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the way the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and I could not heal it;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to go through the limb until the limb was completely lost. 
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another wonder which drains the festering abscess, and then inflames through the malice of its ruler.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a sore, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not fitting that one touch it with iron unless it is in a place where one can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, you must know that manual work is divided into two divisions: 
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work where there is danger in several situations; 
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.  
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary that you protect yourself, so that fools cannot speak badly of you. 
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take up your arms in defense, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised. 
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	And leave curable diseases without sorrow.  
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	And remove your arms from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory. 
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen said in some of his admonishments:  
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not undertake a bad illness unless you are called a fool. " 
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to III chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are of fire cauteries and of medicinal cauteries with water, and the chapters are ordered from the head to the feet. 
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the forms of instruments, and of the bindings for the cautery, and of all that is necessary in the work. 
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is of cutting and piercing, and of cupping and wounds, and of the extraction of arrows, and of similar things; 
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapters are ordered and the forms of instruments. 
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is of restoring dislocations and sprains, and of similar things; 
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered from the head down to the feet, and the forms of instruments.  
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus as we remember the work, it is fitting that I say the quality of the help and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest speech and subtlest science and the most secret reply; 
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and of these spoke many of the wise, and agreed to this; 
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and their words suffice me little, for I fear the length.  
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that the cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions. 
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	That is to say, hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter. 
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, they agreed that the cautery is of great help. 
et li autre dirent le contraire:	And others said the opposite.  
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	That the cautery is of no use for diseases that come from heat and dryness. 
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to treat hot diseases by heat, nor by dryness.  
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And those who said the opposite stated that the cautery is of great help for hot and dry diseases that occur in the bodies of men. 
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it several times by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, do not interfere unless those who have experienced it and who know through long usage the chapter on cauteries, the diversity of complexions of men, and their predispositions and the causes of their diseases, and the outcomes and the space of time. 
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	We have no fear of other complexions, even cold and wet diseases. 
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the mire assembled and agreed to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that the fire cautery together with fire is of the secrets of cures, and of greater benefit than the cautery of burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come near any member but that which is cooked, and does not harm another member no matter how close it is.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning remedies come from one limb to another while driving away, and they bring healing diseases to the limb.  
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And by chance they kill the sick person. 
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire because of its height and the goodness of its substance does not do this, if there is no superfluity.  
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experience and by the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is upon the truth of things. 
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And for this I excuse myself for the length of speech, because it does not please me that I should take away from you the secret which is revealed about fire and the quality of the work, how it drives away diseases from the bodies as the philosopher says in demonstrating.  
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Or receive it in your thoughts. 
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what times cauterizations should be done, and they drew up precepts.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the following harms are alleviated by the aid of cautery.  
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And especially if the cautery is for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait for a time when greater harm may come to the limb. 
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear son, as foolish people do; 
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cautery has no return. 
et il le dient ensi;	and they say so; 
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, because cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion and dries the humors that are the cause of pain, and is worth more than medicine for its swiftness of action, and for the power of its work and its mastery.  
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the illness comes at times according to the patient's complexion, the place of the illness, and its nature. 
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	And if the superfluities are gathered in him through the acquisition of meats and similar things, then cauteries administered in the place where there is excess superfluity and moisture, such as cauteries for pain, and similar things, and the pain does not return.  
mais ce avient poc.	But this happens rarely. 
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last of medicine, and it is as follows. 
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	But they do not believe that cautery is of value after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cautery is the last of medicine because when we administer methods of healing for any illness and they are of no value, then we administer the cautery, and it is effective. 
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then understand well that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauteries of instruments of gold are milder than iron, and they say this only because of the quality of gold and the height of its substance. 
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	And they said that the burns of a cautery do not cause putrefaction, but this is not true because I have tested it and found that it is true in some men. 
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And cauteries of gold are worth more than iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And however when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly. 
et s’on le chaufe trop;	And if you heat it too much.
si font au feu;	It will catch fire.  
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And thus there are enough obstacles. 
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use the fire cautery which we have shown to be suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have ordered this chapter from head to toe so that the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	with olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two ways to do it because of a disease called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and the ears, and because of many dreams and toothache, and throat pain, and even for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a dissolving medicine modifying the head III humors or IV, according to what the virtues and the ailment and the custom of the patient can suffer. 
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the head of the patient fall back. 
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on your thighs;  
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; 
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and where your two thumbs will come, if it bleeds afterward, heat the cautery that is called "olivare", of which this is the form: 
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and move downwards while squeezing your hand bit by bit, turning around;  
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand gently, and examine the spot to see if you see a little bone below;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you don't see it, start the cautery again until you see the bone as I told you;  
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After taking a piece of silk, put it in warm and soft cotton and apply it to the area and leave it for three days. 
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	Then apply moistened cotton buttered.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	And leave it on until the burn is gone. 
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrapharmacon" until it is healed. 
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges.
et por ce si aide mues.	And for this reason, it is aided by movement. 
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one must leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burned, and then cut away what has been burned from the bone, and it should be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that one should leave the cautery on for as long as possible and press it so hard that it sinks into the bone as wide as the spindle that women put in their looms so that the stagnant humors are purged out. 
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	And one should leave the wound open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards one must cleanse and suture it 
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is a way of fear; 
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should leave it out;  
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the shoulder is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other limbs; 
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and especially when the shoulder of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more gentle and moderate for me, and I use this one in all cases to achieve salvation. 
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When in all the head comes chronic pain, and lasts a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie," and purging of the head and oils and plasters; 
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one makes the cautery as we have said before, it is of no value 
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care if the head of the patient is strong and not too cold; 
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize below that cautery a little as we have said above.  
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterward make a cautery on each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery where the place is called "vessels"; 
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is these places where one applies cupping glasses;  
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and align your hand so that you do not see the bone: 
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauteries of the horns be more delicate than those with which one cauters the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes to one part of the head, and the illness extends as far as the eye, and the head is purged by cleansing medicines, and the other cures have been done that I have mentioned in the division of illnesses, and all this does not help at all: 
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Then make cauteries according to two ways, that is to say with hot medicines and with fire. 
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	Cauteries with hot medicines are such that you take a piece of alum, and remove the bark and cut it into a small piece as large as the head, and then place the temple where the pain is in half a manner so that you can put the piece of alum under the skin; 
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is placed, bind it well and leave it like that for twelve hours; 
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then unbind it and apply garlic over the piece of alum, and leave the wound like that for two or three days; 
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then put on cotton soaked in butter as much as possible. 
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment of anointing until it is healed; 
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	And if you see that this is done with any burning medicines which I have written or you may treat with burning medicines.  
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery in the following way:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a bell or it has a small curve, and in the middle a small opening; 
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	And place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and turn the fire a little, so that half of the thickness of the kernel is burned; 
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And remove your hand so the artery does not burn, which is outside, and a lot of blood flows.   
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterward put cotton in oil of cedar and place it on the spot for three days; 
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then he puts softened cotton with butter, and then cures the place with ointment until it is healed; 
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", at the very tip, and beware of cutting the artery in this migraine which is not old. 
de emigraine	from headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you cure migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not profit, and you see that the cauteries previously mentioned of medicine and iron do not suffice, then it is necessary that you sharpen the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; 
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And draw thus on the painful spot a line half an inch long, and remove your hand once, and strain so that you do not cut the artery and do not reach the bone; 
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the mandible that moves when one chews, and the nerves should only be concerned with the movement and that spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of blood flowing from the artery when it is cut, for cutting causes great fear even in him who knows it, and he who is not a student and experienced; 
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work halfway done; 
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is in this book. 
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the middle of the head as we have said, and heal the wound until it is healed; 
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see it, administer the cautery that we have said or chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery which has two knives; 
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And this cautery is better than that one and more helpful. 
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from cold, and one has worked on it with dissolving medicines and other cures as we have said in the division, and the pain does not cease, then heat this cautery which is called "point," of which this is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After pointing all around the patient's ear, or around both where the pain is felt, and you move a little bit away from the root of the ear once you have marked the place to make the incision. 
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	And make 10 points around each ear; 
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area until it is healed.  
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torment which must be cured by cautery is none other than those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases. 
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	And do not perform cautery on those that seem to come from dryness and spasms of nerves.  
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this kind of torment that moves from phlegm by purges and gargles, and this is not enough, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one in the root of the ear, and another a firebrand behind the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; 
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make a cauterization on the head of the ear above a spot below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; 
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery on until half of the kernel is burned; 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery: 
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it resembles the knife that we have put forward, but it is a spot more subtle, and it is fitting that the knife be a spot larger; 
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards cure the place as I have said before, until it is healed. 
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not profit, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauterizations: 
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	On the two horns of the head, and one on the head itself, and one on the vein which is called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach. 
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	And let it be cured as we have said before. 
de litargie	Of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, one should give the patient large doses of herbs and pills that modify the brain. 
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	Afterwards raise the head of the patient altogether, and put mustard plaster on the back of the head as it is written or treated in the treatise of plasters. 
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	And this is the manner of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	If you do as I have said. 
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If it is healed thus, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	And if it is not, make him three cauteries from the top of the head descending to the neck, and have a space of two fingerbreadths between each cautery.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and the cure like the others, and if you see it added, and the patient is suffering, then make the cautery in the middle. 
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if needed, two others on the two horns, and the cure until it is healed; 
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cauteries be called "olivary", as I have said before.  
de la froidor dou chief	From the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is fitting that the head be cleansed of herbs and of what we have said before; 
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after shaving the patient's head, then make a cautery on the back of the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; 
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is severe, then make four cauteries on the spine of the back; 
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let him leave it until the most painful part is burned, then lift your hand. 
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After the treatment, while it heals, use the cautery called "olivary" which we have previously mentioned. 
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to modify the brain with herbs and other remedies that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and suffering from a lack of medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot endure it, make him gargle and chew often while modifying the brain with good meats; 
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after he raises the head in the middle, and he makes the cautery as we have previously said, and the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn;  
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is strong and suffers, make him cauteries as I have said to one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let it be the olivary cautery according to the manner that I have said. 
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is feverish, do him a subtle cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by reason of melancholy are the superfluities or moist humors corrupted and gross phlegm, then the cautery of parts cauterizes as we have said to him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy the superfluities are declining towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then let him drink things by which the brain may be cleansed, according to what is stated before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After you examine the head of the patient; 
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	Then make a well-made linen bandage, also like a circle, and place it around the head. 
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	And the patient should be crossed, and held firm in all directions.  
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	Then apply a poultice made of old birch butter; 
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	And warm it gently over fire so that the patient can tolerate its heat.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	Then remove the circle from around the head and let it cool.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And do this for the patient once a week with good governance until they are healed.  
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see that the cauterization is burning too much, make several points with the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery softens the brain properly. 
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	And then apply softened cotton soaked in butter and gelatine fat. 
de l’awe des eulz	From the eye of the eels
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the ill humor first comes as the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and make the patient drink things purifying the head, and protect it from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After he commands the patient to turn their head back and applies a cautery around the head, making two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the ailment is at both ears together or one if the descent is at only one. 
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	And apply the cautery to all the veins and arteries that are below the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; 
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, staunch it with a piece of cloth as you have. 
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in incision the caution with which you will stretch it; 
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And never make a cautery or haste below the two bones behind.  
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or near the arteries that appear on the surface outside; 
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and we see that these are superfluous cold phlegmatic things, then make the cautery as I said at the beginning of this chapter descending to the eyes:  
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I cauterize the head, and I cauterize on the two temples, and I cauterize where it hurts below the two bones. 
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	And if there is more need, I cauterize above the eyebrow with a small cautery.  
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	the body of tears by within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not profit, then give the patient three nights' worth of boiled chicken broth. 
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After he rinses his head, he applies a cautery with olive oil in the middle.  
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	And he makes two cauteries with a cautery called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, a little bit below the hairs. 
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	And be careful of the artery so that you do not cut it.  
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called “clavilis”:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the membrane of the eye is softened by sickness and moisture, then the cautery of this instrument which is called “olivare”.
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see fit, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are. 
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And do not let go of the hand except until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said. 
dou poil qui point l’oil	Where hair points the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hair of the eyes is converted to parchedness, and pricks the eye, and one does cauteries according to two manners: 
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	That is to say, of fire, or of burning medicine.  
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; 
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. 
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they are born and are equal, then put the patient in your healthy hand;  
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	afterwards draw upon the paper of the eyes a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; 
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then he puts softened cotton in egg white and parsley broth on the eye, then he heats the cautery which has this shape: 
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked dot and dot many times, so that the heart is burned at that spot; 
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	And the signs of the success of the work are that you see the paper withdraw, and the hairs rise at the point of the eye; 
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then lift your hand, and leave it like that for three days, then he puts softened cotton in butter until the burn is removed; 
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment with ointment until it is healed.  
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this the hairs come, and the paper is softened then begin the cautery on that same spot, as you did first;  
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if the hairs are absent, cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural place, and it is even, and they do not prick the eye. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The cauteries of burning medicine are such that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and even, then make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf; 
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and quicklime, of each one dram, and grind together well; 
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it quickly so that it does not cool down, then spread it on the shape that you have made like a myrtle leaf, and place it on the paper over the hairs; 
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	And if the ailment resides in one eye only, then you should work on that one, and if in both also;  
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put under the eye moistened cotton steeped in egg white; 
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	And the head of the patient be in your hand and put your finger showing on the medicine and press it a little and lift all the time that the patient feels a bite from the medicine for he will feel a bite as of fire. 
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the bite has passed, lift the place of awe and see if you see the paper lifted as it was lifted by constraint of fire or by incision; 
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, put more of the medicine on the place where the medicine has not worked until your works are equal and your eyes are set in place; 
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put softened cotton in butter until the burning heart is gone, then heal the place of anointing which is called "dyafenis" and others until it is healed.  
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to guard yourself well at your work with great care so that no part of the medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then begin the medicine again on that place which is softened by the paper properly, just as you did before. 
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the cure until it is healed; 
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And this is the form of the cautery made of myrtle:  
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	Know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to that be your constraints; 
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And let not the right way be withheld from him whose study is this art. 
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the healing of a fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then it is necessary that you burn it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in your lap;  
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	And hold the minister's head between your hands in such a way that he does not move or turn his head; 
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	Afterward, put softened cotton in egg white or parsley juice on the eye;   
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After you heat the cautery which is like this: 
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	And it is shaped at the tip like the form of a swallow's feather, together with which is the cautery; 
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	If you see, if it is pointed from one tip to the other, and if you see, if it is also like a tent; 
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	But nevertheless, this which is shaped is worth more for your work.  
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the fistula if it is open, and drawing out the corruption, and drying it; 
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	And if it is closed, so work on it, and draw out pus from there;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	After put the hot cautery on it, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part where there is no iron on top of the eye, so that your hands do not tremble;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	And put the cautery in the fat of oil, and corrupt it. 
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the beginning of the cautery to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, start the cautery again one more time, and another if you need it, and leave it for 3 days. 
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	Afterward he puts it on softened cotton in butter, and cures it with a drying ointment until it is healed, and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, put an aqueous corrosive medicine on it until the bone is uncovered.  
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	And let the king rule according to what would come in his chapter. 
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand a fistula, and make the place;  
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Afterward put in the fissure a subtle linen thread of which this is the form: 
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	And make it to the quantity of one third of an inch;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand or the thread firmly, and let neither the patient nor anything move so that the melted lead does not run to its oil; 
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	And it is necessary to put moistened cotton on the patient's eye in wine or ale. 
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The plum tree heals the place of a fistula and the healthy one by marvelous health. 
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer a poultice to the nose, and bring the fistula back into the body according to what is appropriate in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	of crevices in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks happen in lips which are called "hairs", and likewise in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds of which we have spoken in divisions, and the treatment does not profit, then heat a small surgical cauterizing knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And put it hastily into those crevices as far as the fontanel.  
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, cure the place with wax until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes in the root of the jaw or in the eye, or palate, or at the roots of teeth, after it is rotten and red and swollen and becomes a fistula; 
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	And you cure it as we have said in sections, and it profits nothing. 
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	Then it is necessary that you have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	After you burn or pierce the hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron heats up,
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do so once or twice, after the treatment of what we have said in treatments, until it is healed. 
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	And if it is treated thus, it is good; 
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	And if not, it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter. 
dou movement des dens	with the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine and that does not work, then put the head of the patient on your lap; 
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	afterwards heat the cautery in the manner that will be shown hereafter so that you put a cane on the tooth; 
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and quickly insert the hot cautery, and hold it as long as the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; 
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	afterwards lift your hand and start the cautery again according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After the patient fills his mouth with salt water, let him hold it for an hour and then spit it out. 
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was moving is made firm, and the softened gum restrained, and the corrupted moisture dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold, or there is coldness or wind, and medicines are not effective, then it is necessary to use a cautery in two ways: 
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Butter cautery is such that you take butter from a cow and place the end in an iron or silver spoon; 
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent peg, soak it in boiling butter, and place it on the aching tooth quickly and hold it until it cools down. 
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and do this often until its power reaches the root of the tooth; and if you see that soaking wool and cotton in cold butter and placing it on the aching tooth, and then putting a hot iron on it until the fire reaches the gum of the tooth.  
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cauteries with fire are such that you take a piece of iron or wood, and it is thick so the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient;  
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	Afterward heat the cautery, from which the shape will come after, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; 
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next. 
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the haste of that cautery, and then refresh it further; 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery: 
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery of any shape that you wish, and according to what you have power;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the shape of the cane:  
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofula is caused by phlegm and cold moisture, and does not yield to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery head with which the following form will come, and have two openings for the smoke to escape from the other side of the cautery.  
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	And apply the hot cautery to the abscess once, or where it is needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess. 
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	And if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess and leave it thus for three days. 
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	And place softened cotton soaked in butter on top until the burn is gone.
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed. 
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cautery:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture overwhelms the channels of the body and also when it arises from a cold complexion, then the patient should first be purged by dissolving medicines. 
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After you apply the cautery to the root of the throat, and be careful not to go near the throat, and only burn where the heart is but it's a prick. 
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After you apply the other cautery at the juncture of the neck and head of the spine, and it is the cautery which is called "clavile" as we have the form in front. 
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat the place as we have said before until it is healed. 
de la toust	From the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and illness of the porcupine is from cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor thirst, and the illness is old, then you make two cauteries on the thigh in their hollows.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	And the other cautery place it between the two nipples. 
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	And let the cauteries be called "clavile" according to the form that has been said before.  
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see it, make a cautery by pricking with the whole cautery which is called "point," whose form is shown above in the illness of the ears; 
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And let the points be up to XXX, or thereabouts. 
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the place according to what has been said before, and let the cautery be three fingers long according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because of this, the cauteries are lighter, for you make three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then it is necessary that you first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards have the patient lie on his back and on his side; 
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	afterwards lift the heart that is within the nipple with the two fingers of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inside, then heat the cautery which has two nerves so that it is in this form: 
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the heart until you pierce it as far as the side, and the figure of the cautery together with four cauteries would come; 
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason, it is done with the cautery which has three nerves, so that the figure of the cautery is six cauteries; 
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and they are nerves according to the subtlety of a tent and it is the shape of the cautery that has III nerves: 
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never is it applied upon this nerve because there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After put on the cautery with bristles ground with rope; 
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after make the patient rest and do not move the limbs for a long time until he is well comforted. 
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which rarely happens, then make a cautery on the thick part of the clavicle, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and much moisture come to the stomach so that it is drawn out of its complexion, and phlegm is multiplied in it, and accustomed cures are used and they do not profit, then it behoves that the patient be turned onto his back, and extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Then make three cauteries one below the spoon of the foot for the quantity of a penny, to all the cautery pointed, and two cauteries behind the two sides so that the shape of the cauteries is at three angles, and has a half space between one and the other so that they are not joined together when they will rot; 
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauteries be so perfect that they pierce the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries according to this form without adjustment:  
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; 
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	And he who will fear this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach in one place according to the quantity that you see fitting; 
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	Then cauterize with the whole cautery which is called "points." 
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound we have had before, as long as it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver comes to pain from cold and moisture and great flatulence, as long as it is forced out of its natural complexion by superfluities; 
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	And the patient is cured of this as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit him, then it is fitting that the patient be raised up on his backside; 
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and sign three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, avoiding the hypocondria, where the sides of the stomach come; 
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and let there be a space between each cautery the thickness of a fingernail. 
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	And let the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press your hand too hard on all the cauteries; 
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	And only half of the heart should be burned, and let the patient stand upright on their feet; 
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if they cannot, let them lie down, extend their legs, and lift their arms;  
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form: 
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you wish, you can cauterize these cauteries with a knife blade, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn the whole heart, for you would dry up the whole body; 
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let it not reach the bowels, for the heart is very delicate in that area, and you will know by seeing. 
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: 
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too strong; 
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, he feels very sharp pain. 
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment requires purging, it is necessary that the patient be shaved on his head; 
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then mark the place where the abscess is, and then heat a cautery that resembles a ray, of which this is the form: 
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the flesh is burned, and comes to a boil, as long as the pus is all drained out; 
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the cure according to the cure for abscesses until he is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And it is not fitting that anyone should use this cautery except those who have long studied in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured many times. 
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly work, and all the same it seems to me that it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one must make cauteries from the roots of aristoloche, and in this manner: 
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristoloche long, the largest that you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your arm; 
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	And steep it in oil, and hold it in the fire, and cauterize with the cautery between the collarbone and the shoulder, and two small cauteries a bit lower in the part that is below the beard; 
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, sloping back a bit; 
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cautery under the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two others on each side of the breast behind the cautery that is between the two shoulders; 
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	And do not press your hand at all, but make it open as when smelling. 
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancients said that no man should use a fire cautery resembling a razor, and they heat it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to the abscess; 
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and the pain jumps, as we have said in the liver abscess.
