Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	from the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the illness of the mouse according to the divisions of the cures that we have said, and it does not profit, then there are three ways of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Of which there is a way so that you make III cauteries, or IV, in a line according to the length of the mole, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have said before; 
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand at all on the whole cautery, and let the patient often turn onto their back;  
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another way of cauterizing is that you heat the cautery which has two points, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder;  
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and lift the heart which is placed near the mouse, where the pains of the patient come from the left side, and let the elevation from which you lift the heart be according to the length of the heart, according to the length of the body, and let the cautery be according to the width of the body 
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	Then he puts in the two inflamed nerves until the heart is pierced on the other side, and then pulls out the cautery, and thus he will have four. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see, that cauterizing with all the cautery has three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has had decay for a long time, this is worth more than the other cures previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not effective for dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes."
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not profit at all, then it is fitting that you make four cauteries around the shoulder, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the mouse, and two behind the back on the spine, and one near the breast; 
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and let the cautery be very close to the thick of the heart 
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	Then leave the cautery uncovered for a long time to prevent rot, and do not let the wound of the patient heal after the cautery; 
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	and healing will hasten, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God.  
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The shape of the cautery for the belly is the one that we have shown before; 
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	and the ones for the back are olive-shaped, as it has been put forward before.  
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsy and are full of yellow water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; 
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.  
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply with the point, lest you burn the yellow wax, and let the cautery be of this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	After make two cauteries on each leg at the point of the knife; 
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	And let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; 
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	And leave the cauteries exposed for a long time without cleaning, so that it dries up; 
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	after the treatment of the other treatments that we have mentioned. 
de la menoison	From the mansion
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When a stomach ailment comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retaining and digestive powers which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and it cannot be cured by any manner of treatments; 
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	And you see the patient suffering greatly and with strong greenness, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the stomach cautery or the circular cautery; 
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	And four cauteries around the elbow, subtle to all one cautery clave subtle, and two cauteries on the thighs. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, then cauterize him on the shoulder, and cauterize each vein, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is profitable when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When hemorrhoids are at the foundation, one or several, and they are old and consist of large cold and wet corrupted humors, and they are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit, then make cauteries. 
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	Three on the spine of the back, those which are all beneath the scapula bit by bit in a triangle shape, and one cautery beneath the elbow two times.  
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	And if you think that his stomach is cold and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then on the face one large cautery on the stomach as it is previously said, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the subtle cauteries. 
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	and let the cautery remain open for a long time. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the place so that it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you apply the cautery, heat it until it resembles a razor, and then place it glowing hot on the cauterized area. 
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	And leave it there long enough so that both your hand and the cautery reach the beginning of the vein, where the blood will be cut.  
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	Do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of cauterization to be done, cauterize each one as we have said. 
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	After the cure of eye ailments, take advantage while they are healthy.  
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	And if you cauterize with a large cautery on a sore, it will be of greater help. 
de plaie mal curee	from a poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or incision, which we will describe in their place, then comes a certain illness that can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When any fistula comes, and is old and has putrid decay and corrupt moisture, you must test its depth with a subtle probe, and make sure that you know the total depth of the probe.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heating the cautery until it resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to the amount the pus has entered, and repeat the cauterization as many times as it takes for the dead and corrupted flesh to be burned, once or twice or thrice, depending on the amount needed.  
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	And beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins. 
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and to the intestines, beware of these places, and do not make this fire except in a fleshy place, and think that it is not dangerous; 
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After healing the place until it is healed, and if the place is cleansed, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed; 
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	And if the materials are not removed, know that the place is infected, and it corrupts the bones at the bottom; 
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	and as one of these that we will say in its place.  
de la maladie des reins	Of the sickness of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain from cold comes to the limbs, and from great windiness, and does not take pleasure in a woman, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the limbs on one side and the other with the pointed cautery that we have said before; 
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	And if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will provide greater help. 
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the back part above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic region begin, and there are right and left, and let each cautery be as long as the nail of a finger. 
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	And make one cautery on the back, or two if you need them.  
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	And let the cauteries be shaped according to the form previously mentioned. 
de la marris	of the sea
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the womb is cold and moist, and does not allow conception at all, and the flowers are corrupted and their endings are delayed;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, there is great pain. 
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	Then it is necessary to make three cauteries around the shoulder, as we have said in the bladder cautery, and two cauteries behind the back. 
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	And let the cauteries be sharpened, as we have said. 
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When viscous humors descend to the hip socket and for this reason it moves out of place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together. 
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	And the place of the two parts is found, if it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip socket with one cautery resembling a circle, and mark in front of the place around the socket as it returns so that the socket is inside the circle. 
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	And let the cautery be such as those with which we have cauterized the stomach. 
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if this cautery is not present to you, make three large olive wood cauteries, and let the cauteries be as perfect as all the hearts. 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cauterize until it is healed. 
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes in the hip bone, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division and the cure is worthless, and the illness is old: 
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	then it is necessary that you purge the patient of the gross humors with foul-smelling pills or other good-seeming pills. 
Aprés li fai cautere;	Afterward, cauterize them;  
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the manner of the cauterization is according to two manners: 
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	that is to say, together burning medicines and fire cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is according to many ways, of which some are like this: 
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	That you cauterize on the hip bone III triangular cauteries according to this form, and make good depth and large, and have between each cautery space the thickness of a penny, and let the cauteries be olive-colored; 
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Once done, one cautery is made in the middle on the head of the hip, for which there are IIII according to this form: 
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see, if the cautery at the cautery of the circle that we have previously said in the dislocation of the hip; 
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	But make in half a manner so that the circles contain all the hip, and all the kinds of bone are burned.  
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it comes down to the thigh and leg, make II cauteries there where the patient says the pain holds him, and I cautery above the ankle IIII pennies, on the left side a peck; 
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	And let the cautery blade be sharp, and burn the thickness of a heart. 
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers or near it, then cauterize him where he feels the pain three or four times with a cautery called "points". 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if necessary, do more.
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if he knows that the pain is below the knee toward the thigh, then cauterize it with a blade-shaped or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauterizations so that you do not leave the cautery long enough to burn the nerves and large arteries, and so that you do not cause the patient greater pain and contraction. 
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen several who have performed cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it until the leg was all swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of the belly from which he had death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cautery in one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the wise say of cautery of the hip, which is as follows: make a tool like a nail, as thick as a doctor's thumbnail or a little less, and with spaces between them, from one space to another the width of a thumb knot. 
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and let the handles be opposite each other on two sides, and also shaped like ours, and it shall have one iron handle well made. 
et c’est li forme:	And this is its form: 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And let it be heated until it is all red and gives off sparks, and then put it on the bone of the sick hip, and turn it on the healthy side. 
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and let the cautery be done once the cautery iron is red hot and leave it for three days.  
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	And then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time.  
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment with anointing until it is healed. 
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasim says that we use this cautery little because of fear of its appearance, and few are seen to use it. 
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and nevertheless it is one of the good cauteries, which he who can endure it, and where it applies itself
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The burning medical cauteries are such that you make the instrument with spaces in which the edge of the door descends, and it is made of bronze or iron with a long side, and at its height there are two grooves, and between each one there is the quantity of the thickness of a thumb; 
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	And they are open above and below, and they join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	Afterward, put the box of the hip on the patient lying on his sound side, and press your hand very hard on the box of the hip; 
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Then put between the two circles of the hot awl which is heated in the fire for a moment, and leave it there for an hour or so, and let the patient suffer the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For it brings a bite as well as fire; 
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	and when the bites have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hip with warm water, and leave it like that for three days, and put butter on it until what is black from the burn is removed 
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and leave it for three days so that decay is drawn out 
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and this would be the last help after the treatment of ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, make the instrument that has warm water according to what you did on the hip similarly;
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and this is the way of warm water, and I have written it or treated it in the treatise of the rectification of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot coals, as much of one as of the other, and crush them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	where there is a small opening where the point of a razor can enter;
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and put then that pot or another pot well-sealed, and put alkali and lime and soft ash on top, as long as there is one to two finger widths of powder so you will have it well prepared in your hand. 
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and leave it like that until the ash descends and gathers or in a sealed pot, then take all that ash and pour it on lime and alkali as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then it will be very caustic and is administered in many medicinal works and for cauterizing other members.  
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it does the work like fire, and with other medicines with which one cauterizes well the hip thus as turpentine and honey of Anacardia and lime with soap, all these things mixed together. 
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galien tells us of a cure by which a man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic vein, and praised it greatly, and said that no other cure was done, and that he was healed at once when this cure was done, and he bathed himself as he teaches it here afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And say in this way that you take two parts of green vitriol fresh and dry, and grind it very much with a bit of fat, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain resides, and bind it; 
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And let him leave it for three hours, so that the patient no longer feels the burn. 
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put it in a bath as long as his body is warmed up a bit, and put it in bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a cautery of such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of humors.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat droppings, it helps a lot. 
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And it must be done in two ways. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and put it on the joint that is between the thumb and the finger which is called the knuckle.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	Afterward, take dried goat droppings and ignite them until they are charcoal, then put them on wool and leave them until they are extinguished. 
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	And do it again in the same way and do not stop doing so until you think by feeling that it has reached the hip, and the pain has ceased. 
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	And this method of cauterization is called "goat dropping cautery.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or by percussion or by excessive evacuation, or by similar spread of cold matter, none of these conditions warrant cautery except for that which comes from infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is fitting afterwards that the patient be purged with fetid pills or other similar ones, which are applied to his back, where the pain lies, three lines marked in an inch, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure.
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and let the cautery be done according to the cautery which is called "points"; 
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see fit, make III or IV cauteries with a medium-sized clavichord cautery according to this form: 
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight anal sphincter when they get up, and fear; 
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you will find in the last vertebra of the back and in us the appearance that comes upon the other vertebrae.  
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it cleansed, if you cauterize it with a cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery evenly scorches each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, that you cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery making II or III lines, and the points are close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After healing the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and guard that you do not apply cautery in any gibbosity that is in a space of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When joint pains are from moisture that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which the laity properly call "gout", and when it is of a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cautery in this manner: 
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary for you to grasp the face of the foot, if you do cautery on all the cautery that we call "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, which often happens, make cauteries on each knee three or four on each side, all olive-shaped.  
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand still except until the thickness of a grain of wheat is burned.  
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knees and back, apply the cautery as we have described in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist two lines long; 
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if there remains any pain in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part and give good care to the patient and take medicine. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give it good governance and purge phlegm, it will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of a broken bone
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture comes in anger, and the bowels descend to the testicles and it is recent, it is fitting that when you see him cleaned, he does not eat anything that day.  
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	And let him use things that loosen the belly so that the phlegm descends from his belly; 
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	Afterward, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath while the bowels are being repaired, and reset them at your will, and press down below the rupture onto the bone of the hip, and make a sign like half a circle above the body; 
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then heat the cautery which has this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it oozes pus
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then reset the bowels in their place. 
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	And have the assistant hold his hand so they do not return.  
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and work well on the patient's thighs, and put a cushion beneath him and a sergeant upon his thighs, and another upon his foot who will hold his hands; 
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	Then place the cautery upon the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you come to the bone; 
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	And be careful that the pus does not flow out when you make the cautery; 
que tu ne le brulasses;	that you do not burn it;  
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and that by this the patient does not die, or other evils. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is fitting that the cauteries for children be small according to their size, and those for large people also large according to their size; 
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	After three days treat the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed;  
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	After the treatment of other wounds until it is healed, and let the patient lie on their back for forty days so that the wound heals well; 
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that his bandages be loosened for a long time, so that the boils do not protrude when he will get up to go into rooms. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, give him a well-made bandage, and let him wear it for forty other days;
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	And have good rest, so that he does not work much and guards against too much drinking and eating, and against excessive shouting; 
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he follows these instructions he will be completely healed. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the cure of the tailor in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When tumors come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, make a cautery with a cautery iron according to its size, and burn one-third of the tumor; 
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the cure according to what we have said 
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients have said that one must cauterize it with a three-angled cautery according to this form: 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first sign the place of incision and make a line across its width above the fracture, and another behind it, and hold your hand steady with all the cautery heated.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help it, then it should be cauterized with a cautery called "poins", and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and virtue and location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	if it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; 
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	if not, begin another cautery upon the first, for such custom is that it should turn to the limb which is nearest, for which it behooves you to make the cauteries until the patient is healed.  
de meselerie	Of a wound
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The cautery is helped sometimes by great aid, and the same disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	When you see it cauterized, take care if the ailment is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread nor remain, and you doubt that the corruption might spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries upon the head: 
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I apply one hand to the nape of the neck, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair. 
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	And with two hands on the temples, one behind on the shoulder blade. 
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	And I leave my hand until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the crusts come out so that the vapors of thick humors can escape. 
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	And I cauterize on the thigh according to what is in front.  
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the inflammation is scattered everywhere; 
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	And it is clearly losing, then you must cauterize with the cauteries we have mentioned on the head and one on the nape of the neck and two on the spine of the back, and one large one on the rump and another nearby and two on the shoulders. 
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and on the elbows, and on the tendons of the foot, and on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; 
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and beware of the nerves that are on the sole of the heel, lest you burn them; 
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that when you do more cauteries, you do more good, and increase the benefit; 
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	and know that the sick do not feel pain from the cautery as the healthy feel it, because the body is already all corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After curing the wound with flour of vetch mixed with honey and other cures until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling comes in any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb; 
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	And let the cautery be a point inserted into the thickness of the flesh. 
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it with ointments until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And one sometimes makes a cautery with the hand and foot and back, at the issue of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus it is removed. 
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And in all ways let no one interfere unless they are knowledgeable of the limbs and the issues of the nerves that move the body. 
de albaras	From alabaster
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the ailment which is called “albaras” has grown old, and the remedies of medicine are worthless, then cauterize a point with a cautery, according to the quantity of the thickness of the flesh, so that the paleness is removed and its color changes. 
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	Then treat it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of a dove and blood of an almond, of each one part. 
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be mixed all together, and let it be tied with a cloth, and let it air in the place until it is healed 
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of ulcers by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre first appears, and you see it stopping, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And nevertheless the wise say that one should also do cautery in the middle of the ulcer; 
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and nevertheless it does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times; 
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and what is more right is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called a "circle," as we have said in our discussion of cauteries.  
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot move
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has an illness that is called "adubelati," and it lingers because of the superfluity that it causes or because of the weakness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, too old) and he has little blood, or because of time; 
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you will see hasten to die 
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then the cautery surrounds it with many small burns by pricking.
aprés le laisse ensi.	afterwards, he leaves it like that. 
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce all the way through with the cautery, heat the cautery so that it is this shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that ailment which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it behind in some way so that the course of the rot is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment as long as it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another kind of illness which is called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a wasting away of the limbs, for it consumes the limbs just as fire consumes dry twigs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this illness in a place that can endure cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries very small and large, according to what suits the place where the illness is; 
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	afterwards, cauterize on all sides until you eradicate all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything that is corrupted is removed. 
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply cauterized softened wool with oil on top until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the healing of wounds generating flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if after three days you see healthy flesh does not grow, it's good.
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if not, then start the cautery again on what remains corrupted. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this ailment has sometimes been cured with medicinal water instead of fire cautery.
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	But nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for the ague in the division: 
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the leeches which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that at the feet through fire a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding and is a large thing lacking which bleeds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this illness are according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and hot iron cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery is when you heat the cautery iron as much as a raven's feather, and it should be made of good iron to the extent that it can burn the nail from all sides, and that it has subtle edges; 
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After you put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and leave it like that for III days until it begins to rot. 
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Then make a plaster of wild mallows crushed with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. 
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place of ointment spreading charcoal until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by fire the body, and often occurs in hands and feet, it is fitting that you administer a hot cautery. 
et est en teil maniere:	and it is done in this manner: 
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	Take a cane of iron or a feather quill, and put it on the nail and the heel, that is to say for warts. 
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	And put the cane on so that it surrounds all around, then put a piece of hot coal, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot coal deep down to the root. 
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	And let the patient suffer a bite from the hot coal for an hour.
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	Then leave it like that, and it will uproot itself by all its roots. 
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Then do one after another, until you have pulled out all those that are in the body, then heal the inflammations which breed flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When some tremble from cold of nerves, or from quartan fever or other, it is fitting that you make them four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine. 
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	And one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach with an olive-wood cautery.  
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	This will leave the trembling, and hasten the health from the cold illness. 
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes ulcers appear on the body, or stinking pustules, which come from large corrupted substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	It is fitting at first, when they appear, that one makes a cautery on each head of the pustule:  
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	A subtle cautery from myrtle wood, with which the point is grasped in fire, or of a long aristolochia root, or to a lentil-shaped cautery. 
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And one cauterizes them at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further, but are broken down from the superfluity whence they come, and are healed. 
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	But it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the forefront, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cautery of a limb, and similar things. 
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	And it is a very grievous thing to staunch. 
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, if you hurry to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press very hard until the blood is quieted under your finger, and no drop issues anymore. 
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	Then put to the fire olive-wood cautery irons, small and large, until they are all red-hot;
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take one, large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is severed, and put the cautery on that vein where you are holding your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is restrained.  
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your hand from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not cease to do one after the other until the blood is drained. 
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	And be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient. 
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And know that when blood flows freely from the artery, it cannot be well cauterized, especially when the artery is large, unless it is done in one of the four ways we have described. 
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	Either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by a strong ligature of thread, or by medicines placed upon it which have the power to staunch blood. 
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And let it be bound and tightly restrained. 
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will apply ligatures tightly with bandages or put burning things on it, or other similar things, it will not be profitable and will do harm.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to anyone and they do not have a mirror or medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it is staunched both on the wound and on the vein. 
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	And do not move the joint, but moisten it with cold water as often as possible until the blood is frozen and thickened and rested. 
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And make incisions ahead of those for which he needs to cauterize and use medicine. 
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of cures of the side
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have told you in the first chapter all illnesses in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and the incisions, their causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries. 
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	And I have put this chapter from the head to the feet, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that one can more easily find what one wants. 
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this one, it is fitting, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than the first one of the cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	Where there is doubt and fear, and many die. 
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	There are some who become so distressed by their illness that they die easily because of the intensity they feel from their illness and its severity. 
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And one must fear these things.  
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And there are some who give you their sense and say: 
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am cured." 
et li maladie est despitouse.	And the illness is treacherous.  
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	You should not consent to those who come to you in this manner, but place greater trust in your honor than in your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely with those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can take oaths. 
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	And use prognosis and indications in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored;
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you to acquire good renown, and glory, and long remembrance. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And I have ordered this chapter in divisions by chapters, according to what it is before this chapter of cauteries, that I have divided from the head to the feet so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	sharp head full of pain
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this ailment often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls the child's head too forcefully.  
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	And sometimes it comes from a cause unknown. 
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this ailment in anyone but children, and in all those I have seen, death quickly followed.  
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And therefore it seems to me that it is better for me to leave this work to those who can cure it. 
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose shoulder was filled with pain, and whose head grew larger each day until it could no longer support it. 
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	And the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture gathered below the bone on top of the scapula, between the heart and the bone.  
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and if the work is such that the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should cleave a wide slit between them. 
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and it should be as long as two fingers, so long as the moisture runs; 
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and see this form of the spatulate instrument:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker and the abscess larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross like this:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and you see signs that the corners of the head are open on each side, and the sharp point springs back when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not answer to you: 
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	then you must cleave three slits between the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After extracting the slits with cloths and powders, apply wine and oil and leave them so until the fifth day; 
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then loosen it and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the head be extracted evenly, and have the patient eat dry meat free of moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another manner of incision is that you look where the size of the abscess appears, and the gathering of the point. 
car aucune fois est elle devant;	For it is not always in front.  
aucune fois derrier;	Sometimes behind. 
aucune fois en destre;	Sometimes to the right. 
et aucune fois en senestre.	And sometimes to the left.  
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Therefore make the incision where the abscess appears, and according to the gathering of the point, and let the cut be according to your power. 
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	And beware that you do not cut an artery.
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	And let it flow blood so that the patient does not die from loss of blood and evacuation of moisture. 
de reume	Of rheumatism
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or breasts, and the illness is old, and medicine does not help at all, then the last resort is cautery with which one sears the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	Therefore it is fitting, when you see them cut, that the patient puts his head back. 
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	Afterward rub the area with a coarse cloth until the arteries appear, then draw the patient's neck tight with the whole cloth. 
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look where the vein beats, and its strands from one and the other are after the ears, and they are filled. 
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then sign the strands of its edge, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts, as far as the vein reaches the bone, and this be by the wide space of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see it, put the spatula under the artery and the cup above, cutting as much as it should through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if the blood flows continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not appear to the touch, it is fitting that you measure the quantity of space of three fingers, then sign its edge and cut as far as the bone; 
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and the quantity of blood that it is fitting to let out is six ounces, and perhaps a bit more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the fullness of the artery; 
puis regarde la plaie:	then look at the wound: 
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	if it remains on the bone pointed with pus, cut it so that no abscess follows, then dress the wound and bind it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
de emigrainne	from emigration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes and acute catarrh, due to moisture from tears and the heat in the temples, and old head pain and similar things, and it is treated by medicinal remedies and all that does not profit him, then we should extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the way to extract them is such that the patient makes a raised area behind the hairs of his temples, and listen for the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is little filled except in some men who are too cold; 
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	And if it is full, the patient should tighten his neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and raise the area with hot water until the artery appears clearly; 
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then take the speculum of which this is the form: 
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	Then scrape the skin slightly until you reach the artery, then lift it up with forceps, and separate it well from the tissues that are beneath it on each side; 
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	And if the artery is thin, turn it to the point of the hook, then cut from that part according to the quantity of the two cheeks. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not copied, so will it not jump at all without doubt altogether.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And draw blood for six ounces, down to three. 
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	And if the artery is large, it is fitting that you tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread so that decay does not come before the suturing of the wound, and blood flows. 
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then cut away the excess between the two ligatures at that very hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize with a blade cautery down to the bone so that the flesh is severed.
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And this is the gentler operation if the patient does not have a fever and he is of a warm complexion.  
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For cautery helps to end moisture: 
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	for this reason it is of greater help against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	When it is fitting for the extraction of arteries that one fill the area with old cotton and put well-made tents on top; 
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are unbound, let them be treated with dry medicines that promote flesh growth, and bandages, until it is healed. 
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the artery is cut as much as you work on it, hurry to cauterize it, or apply vitriol to the spot and press it with your hand until the bleeding stops. 
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	And if you don't have this, place your thumb on the spot until the bleeding stops, then apply something very cold to the area until the bleeding ceases, and it is removed as needed. 
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And the best and easiest way to remove an artery is to cauterize the vein with a two-part trenching cautery, but make sure the trenches are well spaced to retain heat longer. 
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And there should be a thumb's width of space between the two knives. Then, when you have marked both spots, place the hot iron on top until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and let them be spaced between the two heads for it is not soldered by this cautery at all. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the form of the cautery: 
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes descend from the veins that are above the temple of the head, and no remedy of medicine profits him, and you see the face of the patient reddening, and feel his forehead swelling as if trembling; 
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and if the areas are tense and moist so that the hair of the papers is shed, and the papers are scorched, and parched by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is needed.
