Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "the bruised cure," and it is that you make behind the patient who has this illness the hairs that he has on his forehead, then make him three cuts on his forehead equally according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the incisions be as it should be all along the forehead down to the nape, and the others as it does to the ribs above the papers, and beware of cutting the arteries which are at the sides above the papers; 
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and let each wound be three finger-breadths wide across. 
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have ready a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping away the blood, then put the spatula sharp on two sides as follows: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is behind the temple to the second incision. 
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape away all the flesh which is between the two incisions down to all the fascia which is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then pull out this spatula.  
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first fissure, which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, it has this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the sharp side towards the flesh burned at the heart, and the dull side toward the bone, and push until it comes to the middle fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to those until the incision is continuous up to those which appear at the heart, and then likewise make in the middle a split up to the other side. 
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	And then extract the blood equally, and press the place for the blood taken. 
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	Then put in each split a tent of old cotton, and put over cloths moistened in wine and oil and vinegar, and guard that no abscesses come there.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And on the third day untie the ligature, and he applies a large poultice of hot chamomile, then the cure of oil with rose oil, and other cures for which one cures wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	where rheumatism of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When someone has acute catarrh accustomed, and you see those dim and small, and weaken the sight, and the papers burned;  
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hairs stand on end, and when the head is cut off it gives sharp pain, and the patient sneezes. 
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Then know by these signs that those substances and phlegm only come from many veins, and the best cure for it is this. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And command the patient to hold his forehead, then make a large incision between the eyebrows, and another two fingers wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin at the fissure of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be down to the bone; 
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples which move when chewing; 
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then insert between the two edges of the fissure some old cotton, and linen bandages; 
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind cloths moistened in wine and oil on top, and beware of a hot abscess; 
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, you must rub the bone until fresh flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that promote flesh growth. 
En teil maniere:	In this manner: 
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of wheat flower, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster.  
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	And administer it to these wounds to encourage flesh to grow all over. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Anything that aches in the ears is one of four things: 
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	either grain, or beast, or stone from a mine or similar thing like iron.  
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils 
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing thing such as water and easily similar things.  
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or something else that doesn't fit in the ear lodges there, and it doesn't grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then apply a drop of oil of violets or oil of sesame, and then proceed to extract it. 
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	And make him sneeze by a certain method, and pinch his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and hold the ear above. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times this cure comes by force. 
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come by force, administer extraction with subtle pincers, of which this is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it jumps out by force with the pincers, that's good.
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	If not, administer extraction with a subtle awl of small double-edge. 
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	And if it does not jump out by that, make a needle of iron and push the point of the needle or the hole of the ear strongly, and fill what is around the needle with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter with the needle.  
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then treat it by force, because many times it comes by force as we have said. 
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	And if it does not come by force in any manner, take glue like that which is used for birds, and put into some instrument which is suitable for doing this, and put a piece of cotton around. 
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the buttock onto the stone or whatever it may be, and draw forth force. 
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not come forth from all these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear just as a hot abscess may vein and spasm; 
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	And the manner of the incision is that you first make the patient faint from cephalic bloodletting and extract some blood according to the measure of his strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upward, making a small incision at the root of the ear in the fat or where it depends;  
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the incision be as round as a crescent moon until you reach the bone, then suck out the pus according to your ability, and quickly suck it into your mouth; 
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and care for it until it is healed. 
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction. 
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it cannot come out, then administer a thin, subtle spatula according to this form: 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grain is damp from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it. 
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	Then extract it with subtle pincers and a suction device, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute pain then when the jaw is inflamed in the ear it is necessary that the patient uses a sneezing of condition first and amples the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the pain is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps further than that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, then take many stones according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and heat them a little in the fire; 
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and place the patient's ear on one or two stones and press upon it with your feet on the other side, and strike another stone upon the stone that is in the ear. 
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop doing this stone on stone until the sharpness has completely gone out, and thus it will all go out. 
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see it, take the joint, and put one of the heads in the ear, and hold the other head over fire until the strongest joint is burned. 
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then make another part of other joints until the sharpness has completely gone out, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of a beast, if it is small-bodied, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division. 
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	But if it is large-bodied so that one can feel it, use extraction with pincers.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	And this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms embedded in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the treatment does not help at all, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun.
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there are any worms, take them out with fine tweezers; and if there are none, take the cane whose shape is this: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	Insert the thinnest end into the ear according to the amount of the patient's suffering, then suck up the whole cane. 
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey and come out, plug around the cane with cotton as I said for the stone; 
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not come out as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven for the killing of worms, and you will find them or their treatment in distillations.  
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, of which this is the shape as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether it is of silver or of iron, three holes are made below for small openings, and above ones for distillation. 
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	And to press the distillation inside, an iron instrument is well made for this, and if you see it take the razor and wrap cotton around the point. 
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	Then put your oil or juice in it, and whatever medicine you see fit in the cane, and the cane is in the ear. 
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	Then insert the razor into all the cotton and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or reaches the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	And let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be somewhat heated over the fire so that it can be distilled into the ear. 
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And make sure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.  
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have a hole in their ears; 
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and the same thing happens to men by rupture of a wound, or by a splinter lodged in the ear, and this rupture sometimes comes completely within the ear, so that one cannot see it; 
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes there is a small fire from the hole, and one sees it well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which then comes completely within, if one cannot see it, is a hidden ailment in various positions, and in this case it behooves you to place the patient's ear in the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside: 
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see an apparent opening, if the work has always this speculum of which this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind, so that it does not crush the ear; 
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the splinter is of flesh or from the earlobe, then hold it with fine pincers and remove it lightly until the whole piece is taken out. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is perfect in the ear, then take a subtle and light razor and heat it a little in the fire, then put it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the splinter which causes pain to the ear, pierce lightly and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear.  
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the hole and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for as many days until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and powder over crushed vitriol.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear is swollen, it is necessary that you remove the tent and insert another tent moistened with cerate which is made of rose oil and wax until the swelling is removed.  
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then care for it until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a flow of blood comes, immerse a sponge and cloths in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the flow of blood which are found in treatises on distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This remedy which comes in papers of the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is fitting that you extend them with forceps and pincers, and the tip of a spatula from its roots; 
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Then put on the place powdered vitriol.  
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without it coming off, then cauterize gently with a lentil-shaped cautery, and cauterize after the incision becomes numb. 
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	And many times repair, so that nothing remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are destroyed and do not return.  
de la gresle	From gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come in papers of the eyes things that seem rough in their shape and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "hail", and it is a collection of moisture thick in the paper above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such: 
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take care if the hail moves from one side to the other, and it is an easy thing to know; 
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Make the bowl quite wide, then lightly scrape each side, then take it with pincers and cut it. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit of the paper, do not worry about harming the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the split is large, sew it together with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; 
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not apply any pressure, for ointments will soon restore it and bring flesh. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the hail is descending inside the ear toward the upper part, turn the paper over and hold the hail with pincers, cut it and press on one side and the other;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not matter; 
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the hail is cut off, wash the wound with salt water and heal the place of the one who complains of flesh as long as the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that gathers in cloths of papers above, and it happens more to children than adults, and it grieves them much in their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; 
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and for this they lie down on their faces immediately, and sleep on them, and are their papers under their eyebrows so wet that it swells and the appearance has covered from the exinach which appears in the eye. 
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exirnach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head in a healthy place; 
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that it contains from each part, then put it on top. 
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your hands on one side and the other so that the exirnach is assembled within the circle; 
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit about as wide, and not any larger than the wound one makes when opening a vein; 
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and cut the skin thoroughly until you reach the exirnach;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in several positions exirnach comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat. 
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Extract it therefore all at once with a piece of cloth pinched between your hands towards the fire, and turn your hand to the right and to the left so that it is scattered. 
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	And make sure you do not put anything into the split, unless you reach all the way to the eye, so that you do not blind it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the pus does not open at the beginning of the split, slightly widen the split until it appears. 
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then extract it as we have said, then wet cloths in water and vinegar, and put them on the area, and bind with bandages. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, then let the healer apply soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow on warts other than those that nature makes and are mature, they harm them and bring about many illnesses such as accustomed tears and softening of the wart and albugine, so long as it is the cause of the destruction of the wart.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And the cure is according to four ways: 
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	either by cautery with fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is before it or the chapter of cautery, and is done either by incision and stitching or by canes, according to what I will say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient on your lap, then turn the paper from the eye to your left hand. 
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is turned over, it is good.  
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	If not, then if you stick a needle through all of it. 
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let this be near the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow near these hairs, and draw the thread over all the paper, and turn it to the razor. 
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	Then make in the part below the paper, below the added hairs, at all the spatula joining, from the large tear to the small one.  
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then extract the thread and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drape, then draw on the paper a figure of an anchor, as the leaf of myrtle, and however it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raising the paper which is divided into all.   
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if one needs to make a large quantity of paper, according to how soft the paper is; 
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then make all the spatula on the two lines that you have signed, and begin with large tears up to small ones. 
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs as thick as a root, then put the awl into one of the two angles of the heart, then skin it all. 
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	Then bring the two lips together with a needle stitch using a very fine thread of wool, and wipe away the blood, and let the excess threads on the two eyebrows dry completely without anything sticky, if you see fit to do so. 
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	And if not, don't worry about it, then leave the stitches and threads until three or four days. 
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then treat the wound without suturing with drying and constricting things, for paper revives at the sewing of the wound and its joining, but the suture is weak (as the ancients say), and this work is done without fear. 
et si a une autre maniere:	And if there is another way: 
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And it is that you cut the paper into a shape like the leaf of myrtle, as we have said, at III ounces dried according to the form which is here:  
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then bind those who overcome small forces equally according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the pliers and the thing is not equal, take a needle with one thread and put it through the shape. 
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	And put one other thread below the large tear, and the second thread below the small one, and bring together between your fingers the threads equally. 
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then smooth your hand equally and lift all the skin on which you have signed, as we have said, then bring together the two edges of the wound by suturing, and treat it until it is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with wax and similar soothing ointments. 
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and it sometimes happens that the hair of the paper is converted. 
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	then you should use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the suture in one and the other is more artful. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The cure of boils is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and that you convert the paper and put it in according to what I have said, then make 2 boils by art, and 2 subtle ligatures as long as the paper and the width of a span is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and take 2 pieces from where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then join one and the other subtly on what protrudes from the paper of the boil, and strain the 2 boils from the 2 parts they form. 
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it like that for several days, and the skin which is strained will die and heal and bear, as long as it seeks by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it delays, if the sore has some strength, then cure it as much as it is healed;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is sewn up, and if the paper is lifted, and the hairs will no longer grow; 
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the work is such that you take a subtle needle, and put a fine and subtle silk thread through it;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then join the shoulders and knot one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; 
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange in the chase the other fine silk thread quickly, and knot the two threads together; 
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then place the patient’s head on your knee; 
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be beneath the sun so that the work is clarified, for this is a subtle and delicate operation, then push the needle all the way in at the root of the hair nearest the joint, and make it pierce quickly through the skin as you draw it along the natural hair. 
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull out the hair up to the joint, and push that hair into the joint, if there is one or two or three or more. 
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out all the way at the joint through the skin with the natural hair.  
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the joint is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull the joint down along the thread that you have ordered, until the joint comes out through the opening above, and you see it with the sight of your eye. 
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then if you treat the wound and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh rises over it. 
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from a horse's mane with it, and let it grow with the one you are letting it grow with, until it is long enough and then remove it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rotting of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this ailment which is called "aleacratio" or putrefaction comes into the eye, there are two ways: 
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.  
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs through the cutting of a wound, or by incision or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way to treat it is that you split open that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put linen threads inside, and bind it until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not fitting that you use anything in its treatment that dries or constricts.  
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than the first. 
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	But work with softening things, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and roses of water or elder and flaxseed are cooked, and ointments of diachylon melted in some oils, and he wraps a tent, and cures it with this.  
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not fuse according to the form it was before. 
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And this work that we have said is nothing other than the direction of this illness, so that it does not return according to the form it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This sickness which is below, which truly is called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	Accidents come from wounds and fissures and cauteries and similar things; 
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of working on it is that you take a needle with a doubled thread and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct as far as the right so that the thread comes out in two sides of the flesh.  
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then place the flesh above all the needle, and the cup at the spatulas width. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is needed, it is good; 
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, take the razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make two fissures on either side inside the paper. 
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	And let the heads of the two fissures be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter which has the name "Greek I"; 
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are below, from what is beneath the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; 
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then follow the cure that we have said of softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.  
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the ailment comes from a fissure or seam or cautery, it is fitting that you cleave a full fissure beneath the hairs of the skin, and according to what is aforementioned; 
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; 
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	And one must do the work according to the form of the ailment, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare all manner of things so that they may make the figure return to its natural form; 
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And the patients themselves, according to what is fitting of work and instruments are in several dispositions.  
dou soudement de la papiere	with the pounding of paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this suture occurs in the hands of men in such a way that the skin above is joined with the white of an egg and cannot move nor do its natural works, then it is fitting that you put the point of a razor beneath the skin, and lift it up;  
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and hold them with pincers, as long as you cut what is exposed with a delicate spatula, which is not too sharp nor too dull, so that the patient can endure that the spatula is not too sharp and does not blind the eye; 
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and your incision, with which you remove the assembled skin, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; 
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and all that is assembled is cleansed, and do nothing at all in the sharp salty eye, and lift it with sweet water, and with coriander; 
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then place between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on the eye wool softened in plenty of egg; 
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day use sweet coriander and other southern things as long as it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that a nail is according to two manners: 
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	It is nervous and seems like hard fat, and another which is not nervous but seems like white frozen moisture, that when one touches it with iron and thinks to pinch it, one cannot. 
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And the one and the other resemblance begins toward the great tear duct, and grows little by little until it covers all the vision and all the light and the movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is such that the patient puts his head in a sound place, then he opens his eyes. 
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	And lift the paper to your hand, then with the point like small pincers, and extend it above;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	Then take a needle and put horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair in it, and strong thread. 
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	And double the point of the needle a little and stick it into the angle, and pierce it with the whole needle, and tie the angle with thread and extend it above, and flay all the hair on the side of the angle which follows the prune and silk to the hair as far as the head, then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with a very fine spatula and with small forces, and leave the flesh natural or tear duct, so that by the incision the body does not usually shed tears. 
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And sometimes they are placed on the oncion alone, and on the thread as we have said; 
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then the skin is scraped off all over so that it resembles this form: 
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, and that the plumule is not pierced; 
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	And after the incision, a piece of silk thread is placed in the eye, and a collar made of pewter, and it is left until the next day; 
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer does what is necessary until it is healed.  
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not sensitive, and you cannot insert the needle, and the oncion cannot enter, many times this type of nail is cured by medicines; 
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and it grows as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, work on the eye of the patient, and take a light sharp spatula according to this form: 
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And raise the splinter subtly, and if you see that it diminishes nothing and the reason hastens it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red lead, and only grind it, and plug the eye until the next day; 
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing else is against it in the eye, such as an abscess, then milk it and first heal the hot abscess until it is healed, then start the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh or tears harms the eye too much, suspend it to the eyelid, and cover one part and not all, so that no body of tears comes in. 
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows upon the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In some men, red flesh is never born, and covers the prunes and holds them on papers and turns them to the fire, and looks like a rose of baluster.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the works are such that the patient puts their head in his healthy side, then he operates them, and all those who have suitable instruments for this, and support with strength; 
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then take the first instrument, and go shaving all the way to the end with the razor, and be careful not to blink at the work; 
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be made in two places as we have said in the incision of the finger and with small forces, which remove the sebum, as the shape after this chapter demonstrates. 
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, apply oil of cypress, broiled, or you can distill red sulfur, and similar corrosive medicines, and put hot oil with a cotton swab soaked in egg white so that it is assured of a hot abscess.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it remains there, and the shoe presses upon it, and you doubt a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess. 
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do as many charts are added to the eye in this manner. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nevertheless, it is necessary that you relieve the treatment of each weak eye from the natural path;  
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from the accidental path, in work with iron; 
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member suffers from this work.  
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red ones that are covered on top of the eye, and endure in sight their work and weaken the eye all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	Therefore, it is necessary first that you look to see if the eye is strong or weak, and there is no other illness except for pain. 
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	Then the boil in a twofold manner:  
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head in a healthy position, then suspend those veins at every ounce according to his wisdom, and let the ounces be subtle doubled according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be applied by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then one coils as forcefully those veins subtly, and wipes the blood hour after hour, as long as you see those veins move away from the eye; 
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and be careful that you do not prick the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only cut those veins; 
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, if you distill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt what remains beneath the eyelid. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you cannot collect all of it in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain is eased and you are sure of a warm abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until he is healed; 
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of force: 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The one named "arissati" makes a fistula.
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you cure it by cautery and burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then cut into the abscess where it should drain, and draw out all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed. 
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed and you see corruption and blackness, then take all the instruments with which its form is:  
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And it is called "sharp chief" and is made of hard iron at the head end and is pointed like a file as it is in the present form: 
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it upon the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a little so that you know that corruption is removed.  
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines. 
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the wound is soldered and flesh grows, and the body of the gut is soldered and remains so for 40 days, and it does not reopen and is not abscessed, and no bad accidents occur, know that it is healed; 
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If this is not the case, if there is nothing else to do but bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this method: 
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and that you uncover the bone the second time with an iron instrument and with sharp medicines; and when it is uncovered, take the drill according to this method, and let the head of the iron be three-angled, and let the drill be thinned down to its point as you see here: 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and keep your hand away from the eye a finger's breadth, then turn the drill completely until it pierces the bone and let the patient feel this because the vein will begin to flow if he holds his hand under his nose; 
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the place, the matter goes to the snow. 
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	This is a lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	From the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eye opens completely and there is no disturbance in vision, nor any dimming, it is fitting that you bandage the patient; 
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then the healthy eye, then apply cupping glasses or a cautery without piercing to suck out [the humor], then put on the eye a plaster made of acacia and aloe and frankincense and sarcocolle, and then strain the eye, and the plaster on top of bandages and cloths; 
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the cloths is such that you take cloths soft enough, and fold each one into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs. 
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then it is strained with a hard bandage, and begin again with cupping glasses to suck without wounding. 
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then remove the cupping glasses and leave the oil strained day and night, and if the ligaments soften, then you must strain it more. 
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then remove the ligature after a day and night, and if you see the oil return, that is good. 
se ce non;	If not; 
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	begin again the plaster and the cloths and the ligature and the cupping glasses until it is healed. 
dou derrompement de toile uvee	For a rupture of cloth with a warp
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruption comes to the woven cloth, then open it, and there will come forth shavings like grains of resin, and it is wondrous to behold. 
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle into the root of the part below up to that above, then put in another needle where it has a doubled thread from the tear duct.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; 
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then take the place of the doubled thread and tie one part of the eye around it, and pull it well, then remove the needle and place a softened linen cloth soaked in plenty of egg white on top; 
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the threads adhere with the eye, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; 
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and once the wound is restrained by the eye on each side of a cloth circle, until it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye has a large appearance, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes perfectly from the eye, correct the white moisture and reduce the eye, and it will enter quickly; 
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healed. 
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bowel of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This illness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing other than a bowel assembled in the eye, resembling descending fire, and this is not fire; 
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	And the manner of appearing in the work is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then take the head between your hands in two parts, and move it so much as you see the bowel come up above your eyes; 
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let it be fixed, and not descend, and let the light be removed, and let the patient see things as he used to; 
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is fire, and if the descending of the bowel is not as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take a subtle spatula and put it on the horny coat in one spot along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horny coat and the corona, so much as the bowel rises;  
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is issued, if you distill in the sharp oil hot mixed with honey, or sharp or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then let it be cured by another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	sharp objects of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have seen the likenesses of the sharp ones in the division, and what it befits for piercing; 
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if in work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It befits that you make the sick one sit between your crossed hands, far from the light of the sun, and bind the sound eye tight very strongly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; 
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda," or in your left hand, if the eye is right; 
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument below the cornea by the thickness of a reed in that part of the eye where there are fewer tears, then insert the instrument which is called "almagda" carefully and twist your hand until it pierces the cornea and you feel the almagda reach the empty space. 
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	And it is necessary that the measure of the almagda passage be equal to the measure from the pupil to the end of the blackness.  
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	And this is the cornea of the eye. 
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you see the bone through that paper because of the clarity of the corneal membrane, then put the instrument all the way to where the point is and then press it down one path after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the point is now lowered, let the patient see it in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	Afterwards rest a little, and if the point goes back up the second path, put force on it with the instrument and when it is well fixed and it does not rise, carefully withdraw the almagda by turning your hand bit by bit. 
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	And then put again a sharp point of a needle gem, and lift out the oil from within it. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply a cloth soaked in rose oil or linen softened in plenty of egg yolk and bind with good oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on a common poultice with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyelids too hard, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit," of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle place, then put in almond, as we have said; 
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And for the completion of the work prepare the patient with a coming doctor, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; 
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	And let him be devoid of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be bound according to his condition until the third day; 
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then untie him in the same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then tie him again until the seventh day; 
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And it does not suit you to do this in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it suits you to delay this, because the sharp point rises quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	When an abscess comes, untie the oil before the seventh day, and dress it with what relieves abscesses. 
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when it is soothed, untie the bandage and put on its face a little gold leaf to cover it for a day, and let it be then in that dark room. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then go out of the house little by little, and convert yourself to your ways;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And know that no disciples should interfere in this matter. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in some parts they made a kind of almond paste, which caused a sharp pain, but even so I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And perhaps it is a new thing. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the resemblances of the forms of almsgiving, so that those who do not know them see them; 
et soient d’arain proprement:	and they should be of proper iron: 
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of these same instruments be of such subtlety, and the last one in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh out of the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes there are born or made various joined chariots, from which there are some that seem like scorpions with many feet; 
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such that have a chariot enchanted with a fox color, and if a chariot of good bone color.  
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In this case then of these chariots which is of good bone and not enchanted, it behooves you to make the sick person sit between your hands against the sun; 
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open their nostrils, and throw the ointment on those chariots, and draw them forth;  
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	for hold it so that you can sustain it with a subtle pointed spatula on one side, as long as you know that the chariot is entirely removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that cannot be grasped, carefully work it out with all the fine instruments so that nothing remains. 
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	And if there is swelling or a pustule appears, cut it as appropriate;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is malignant pustules, hurry and cauterize them until the swelling subsides and all the matter is removed, then pour wine or vinegar gently on them. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If vinegar works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is cured.
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	And if the moisture does not break through as it should, know that there is matter lodged in the bone above which instruments cannot reach to cut. 
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then it is necessary that you insert a thread of linen, rather thick, knotted by hand, and leave a space of a finger or less between each knot.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and place the patient's shoulder on a thread in its nest at the bottom of the armpit, and draw it in smelling as long as it comes through the nose into the mouth; 
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times they do this to the child like schools, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do it;  
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them one after the other as we are on the thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the new ones have corrupted the flesh, then draw the thread, wipe away the blood, and wet the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back to the nest as before; 
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode everything that remains of the flesh;  
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put or place a splint of plank for some days until he is healed, and if he needs drying medications, use them. 
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, in which one distills the oils and medicines or places them: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it is of silver or of iron, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and it conducts also. 
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be filled to purge the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and it has a handle at the head to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquid. 
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh out of the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease called "telul" is born on the head, grows and becomes very large, so that it is dreadful to behold. 
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	And for this reason, you must cut it off at the beginning and remove all the bone, then place a cautery or burning medicine on top. 
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if it is delayed being covered until it becomes large, then beware if it is hard, of dark red color, with poor sensation.
