si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	Do not touch it with iron for it is an inflamed abscess, for when one covers it even once, great harm comes to the patient.  
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	And if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of dark red color, and you see that it can be completely covered, then empty the patient and cover it without fear, and treat the area with drying and astringent things. 
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilaginous operations, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary when this happens to anyone, to see if the wound is fresh and bleeding freely; 
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then join the two edges with stitches, and then treat it until it is healed.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	And if the edges are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape away all the parts of their core until they bleed, then join the two edges with stitches, and remove them, and sprinkle powder made from dragon's blood and ground incense. 
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powders a piece of plaster of Paris or other soldering plaster and leave it until it heals then cure it with anointing until it is healed 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The way to suture is that you bring together the solution: 
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	either with needles as we have said in suturing the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread as I have shown you. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In the hands sometimes appears within the lips of an abscess hard, resembling grains of millet, small and large;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then you must turn back the lips and split open each knot and take them with pincers and cut them in each part
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply oil after the incision of ground glass, until the blood is stopped. 
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then wash with vinegar and treat the area with dry things until it is healed. 
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times flesh boils arise on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; 
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	It is necessary that you hold it with tweezers, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run out; 
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then put powdered vitriol on the spot, or other restraining and drying powders; 
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	And if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize it: 
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes rough and ugly scurf assembles at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, 
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and wormy, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his shoulders be in your lap, and raise the bones or the bark which appear, as long as nothing remains; 
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And then make black and green, and yellow and the other stains, as long as they are cleansed;  
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if you remove that which is at the first reason, it is good; 
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not, start again on the second and third day, until you have raised everything;  
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	And know that the teeth need various forms of instruments to raise them, according to what the work shows, because the rasp with which one raises the front teeth has other shapes than those with which one raises between the teeth; 
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And these forms and others should be prepared for you. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is fitting when you cure a tooth for its pain that you delay as long as you can, for this ought not to be done.  
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	For it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for the removal. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is forced to draw, it is fitting that you are certain of the tooth pulling.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient and he thinks that it is a holy tooth, and causes the good tooth to be removed. 
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	And nevertheless the pain does not depart because of this, as long as the bad one remains, for we have already wanted to do this at these sanctuaries.  
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	And when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is fitting that you scrape around the tooth entirely, and cut deeply to keep the gum from all sides. 
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	Then move it to your two hands or with delicate forceps at the first pinch and pinch, so that it is well loosened, then firmly grasp the forceps. 
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the head of the patient rest upon your thigh between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take any of these instruments and gently insert it into each side, and move it as you did at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the bone is pierced and gnawed, it is necessary that you fill it with cloths, where the holes are; 
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you extract it subtly with forceps, so that it does not break when extracting; 
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to work very carefully around the gum to dislodge the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and a part remains, and the patient suffers greater pain from the root's malice than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not do as the ignorant barbers do, who by their haste and boldness often break the carriage, and do not apply what we have recounted; 
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but they bring about a great illness at times through the roots that remain, or through the carriage that they break, as we have often seen.  
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is drawn, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; 
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if blood runs out, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the place. 
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And if that doesn't work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of the instruments with which one first draws teeth should have long points and thick handles so they do not bend when you draw the tooth; 
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be large members so that they do not bend in the opposite direction, and made of well-made iron, and have teeth to hold the pieces.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains after drawing, it is fitting that you put moistened cotton smeared with butter on the place for a day or two until the flesh softens, then insert the forceps which are called "algefri," whose head resembles a bird's beak; 
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and within they are made like a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say, a small scraper, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps because of this, it is good. 
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, help yourself with all the instruments, from which the following shapes come: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two arms, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools which are before in the manner of teeth, and of this instrument which seems like large pincers, whose form is this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that many instruments are dense.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted. 
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And wise and subtle masters find their own instrument according to what their work and the illness show them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of others, so that it does not break the chariot or other bones, or if it rots, if he seeks the instruments that suit it, as I told you, and help yourself with gestures, of which this is the form: 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-holding to hold the bone so it does not escape, but can hold and remove it. 
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, remove it with all these instruments.  
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When a tooth appears not according to nature and its form is ugly, especially in young women, you should know if the density is born after the tooth and is not in its proper place and cannot be filed. 
adonques lou raie;	Then remove it.
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if it is joined with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak and is made of sharpened steel. 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the saw cuts little by little in the hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears one can file it, then the file of a part files as here is its form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	And it is also like the file with which one makes needles.
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	And then file the tooth bit by bit with your hands lightly so that it does not move until it falls out. 
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	Then smooth the surface at the end with no sharp edge, and if it is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file down the sharpness until it is even so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When a tooth in front falls out, whether by blow or by falling out, and the patient cannot press on what they eat without it hurting, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, and that does not work; 
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then it is necessary to restrict it with a thread of gold, because threads of silver turn green and rot, but gold never changes. 
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And the thread should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you see that the teeth need to be straightened, take a thread and double it between the two sound teeth, then place the dislocated teeth between the doubled thread so that it comes out cleanly on the other side of the sound tooth. 
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then begin again the covering until the place where you started and pull your hand subtly and carefully so that it does not move. 
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the teeth with the thread using pincers and bring them together and place them between the sound tooth so that it does not bite the tongue; 
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave them tightly bound as long as they can remain so, and if they come undone or the thread breaks, bind them with another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it remained and served thus for all its time; and that is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two missing ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, if one puts it back in its place, fresh to fresh, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and no one should interfere who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes one makes the shape of a tooth from a cow's bone, and puts it in the place where there is a missing tooth, and takes it out as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To loosen the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this frenulum which comes below the tongue by nature, one is born like this;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by an accidental wound that has healed; 
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the operation is such that you open the patient's mouth and put your hand on their head, and lift the tongue; 
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then cut the nerve ligament widely, as long as the tongue is loosened from its attachment, and if there is hardness or knotting, which comes from a wound, then insert the hook and cut widely that ligament. 
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	And be careful that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery which is underneath.  
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	And when you have done so, apply a dressing of rose water and alum, or sharp cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen. 
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	And bandage the patient's tongue every night so that the blood cannot coagulate.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, apply powdered vitriol to the area.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	And if the bleeding does not stop, cauterize it with a lentil-shaped cautery, which is good for this purpose.  
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Then the healer continues with other cures until he is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	And if you see it become red, black, or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre. 
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	And if it is turning white and there is moisture, then cut the skin with a fine scalpel and free it from one side to the other. 
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	And if the pus does not come to your work, apply ground vitriol until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you draw out everything completely. 
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then lift the place from dirt and salt, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes boils come inside the throat which are called "godaths", and we properly call them the two almonds, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: 
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron at all. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron either, also for the drainage of blood. 
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	But leave it alone until it is ripe, and then you will cut it open, or it will burst on its own.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of whitish color and the root is delicate, have your instrument ready to cut, but first look to see if the abscess is warm, at rest, and appeased. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, with their hands in your sight, and open their mouth, taking the instrument between their hands, press the tongue down below the whole instrument, so that its shape is seen. 
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And it should be of silver or fine steel like a knife;
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Press your tongue against all these instruments, and you see the abscess, then take the lancet and insert it into the almond, and hold it firmly above more than you can. 
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And draw nothing of the cloths with it, then apply the cup to the instrument, from which this is the shape, that it seems like one force. 
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And all the ways the tips are curved, and one to the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel. 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument, take tongs, of which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And let it be cutting on one side, and not on the other. 
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have covered one of the almonds, cover the other according to this same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, hot and clear, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with hot water, or decoctions of pomegranate rinds are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure it until it is healed; 
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And if any other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two tonsils, then treat them as you would the two tonsils. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had formed in her throat, namely, a small abscess. 
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And it had nearly closed off her entire throat so that the woman could not exhale through the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained in this state for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that he had to put two reins through the two holes of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened therefore and quickly inserted a lancet into one of them, then drew out the pus, and extracted a large quantity of matter.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then I performed the same procedure on the other opening, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue. 
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After you pierce the lancet into these abscesses, and scoop out a part of it, only a little blood should come out. 
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And thus the conduit of the woman's throat was unstopped, and she now began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to lance that abscess for a long time. 
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscess grew again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large. 
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Then I ligated it and cauterized it inside her throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	Then it stopped growing. 
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to her after me.  
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the swelling descends to the uvula, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular". 
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is below large and round, it is called "grape." 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cauterized as we have said in the division, and the cautery does not profit, and you see that the boil has been appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it. 
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round assembled and is not long;  
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is of blood or of purple color or black, then it is necessary that you avoid the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger upon the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue to the instrument of which we have made mention before; 
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the lancet into the grape, and draw it below, and cut with one of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.  
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cut away any more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; 
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	For if you cut away more, it grieves the voice and speech;  
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and care for it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of being cut, you should give him something to dull the fear of the cautery.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and pointed.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And let the patient put his head in good health, and then press his tongue against the instrument that we have said in the chapter on cautery, and hold it with sharp, hot coals, so that it is not too thick nor too thin;  
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in using the point of this instrument, which has this shape: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have on the head a hair or where one puts the medicine, such as the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine upon the eye; 
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and let the patient lie on their side so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine within so that it does not go down the throat and lungs 
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye, the amount of half an hour, until you see it soften and the stinging of the medicine is soothed; 
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument all the way into the cotton above, until the cotton is inflamed on the eye;  
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry and take it out after four or five days.  
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to restart the cautery with medicine, do so, and after the cautery wipe it around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and cleanse what is around it from the medicine. 
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be treated with sharp cold, and be cured by gargles until it is healed. 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, or the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and wormwood and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put water in it, and let it boil; 
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and within the pot there should be an instrument fitted in this manner: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be of silver or iron, and one of the ends should be put into the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is mortified; 
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	Afterwards, repeat often until the eye dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the arrival of the hot abscess, because many things happen; 
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make this fire hotter than the decline of a boil allows. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put inside the head a crust of egg, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; 
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the crust of egg does not make the steam burden the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether healthy. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times a bone or fishbone, or something else gets stuck in the throat;  
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so you must draw out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all your might, so that you see the thing move;  
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; 
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	if perhaps it extracts the thing by vomiting; 
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread; 
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; 
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the place, it will air out, and then you will pull hard;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come easily as we have said, then take an instrument of lead according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	Let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised up; 
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest it suffocate him, and do not push the bone in; 
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument in, so that he knows where the thing is lodged; 
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the bottle is empty, or if it draws the instrument equally strong, until it is strong. 
de la sansue de la gorge	From the bloodletting of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes medicine is without blood, as I have said in the division by the treatment of medicines.  
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And when that does not profit, then look into the throat of the patient in the sun, and press their tongue to the instrument as I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinew, cut it with very small forceps or with subtle tongs that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a hollow reed, and put it into the throat of the patient, then put the end of the reed on a hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And hold the patient with sharp pain every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take a full view of sharp cold and work the mouth and swallow it in a sense and move it with your hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And as soon as the blood feels the cold it will stop. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not stop as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida at the instrument as I have said in the fumigation of the grape.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will fall without delay. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the way of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are live coals, and it is covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and the head of the instrument is put through that hole. 
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then you give the patient the fumigation and they put the head of the cane in their mouth, and close their mouth so that the smoke doesn't escape but comes up to the sinuses; 
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And the sinus will now drain, and if it doesn't, you repeat the fumigation many times; 
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient should endure thirst, and eat salty things and such, and not drink any water; 
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And then it will be necessary for it to drain freely by this treatment.  
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the sinus is, when it can be seen, like curved forceps to be inserted into the throat.  
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And it should resemble a soignee beak, and it should have the roughness of a file, so that whatever it takes hold of, it cannot let go. 
et vez ci la forme:	And see this shape:  
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many abscesses are similar, according to what memory brings here of one and the other in this book, and they vary in perforation and size. 
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	And it is in two ways, one of which is in its own appearance, and from the moisture it holds.  
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those wounds which are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the buttocks, and abscesses of fleshy areas are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And abscesses should not be pierced until the swelling is mature according to its fulfillment. 
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and they do not die according to their fulfillment, such as abscesses that are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it is rotten around, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, by which there is a cause for contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	If the abscess is near a main limb, and you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the main limb.  
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	if it is located near the foundation, if you pierce it, so be it that he dies; 
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not fitting that you pierce an abscess raw without digestion being completed, except for the one that is located near the foundation, lest it rot completely through and become elongated within, and a fistula arises; 
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and it cannot heal in due time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is fitting that you know the time of perforation of the abscess which is dead according to its fulfillment, and that is when the pain is eased, and the departure of fever, and the lessening of pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; 
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is fitting that you make the perforation where the most dependent part of the abscess is located, and where it appears to move; 
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it be the perforation along the length of the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equals where there is no weeping. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the member which is bent.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in fleshy place, it is best that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before this, the venom will spread along the length of the body and is full of much filth. 
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	And by chance the lips harden and its depth. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is fitting that you treat small abscesses, small openings;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large openings, and many fissures according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; 
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is fitting to cut out the core, and cover.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When it has become as yellow as draperies, and is dead, then it is fitting to do as one does for buboes: 
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are some that are split into three angles, and if there are some that we cut like the leaf of myrtle, just like abscesses of angers;  
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are some where we make a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those that do not have a head, such as a superficial boil, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; 
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary that when the abscess is large, and it has collected a great deal of pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain a part; 
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then open the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing at random;  
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times gradually, until all the pus is drained; 
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	the same applies if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman bearing [a child], or young children, or old men decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes the intestines jump out with the issue of the bowel, and by chance the patient dies, and you do not notice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if wipe the wound, and look whether the wound of the abscess is small; 
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a large opening, if apply bandages of linen or fine cotton; 
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put in each one a bandage so that they come against each other; 
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have stitched it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or rasping of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; 
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the bone set, and treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water quickly and easily, wet a cloth, and put it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the discharge of blood persists, apply dressing and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is a time of winter, and the flesh or abscess is very nervous, it is necessary that you put on bandages and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil; 
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it is in summer, and the flesh is thick, then you should place wet cloths soaked in vinegar and oil or in cold wine and oil on top, until the third day as we have said. 
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then untie the abscess, wipe it and dress it as is appropriate, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this should be universally known in the treatment of abscesses:  
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	As I have told you how one must proceed before treating abscesses, see this chapter. 
des soros	of serums
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When boils appear on the head, they are like little pouches of pus, just as the jeweler's pouch for a ring, and there are many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and others that have moisture as well as pus; 
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are some that are hard and stony at the waist, there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist are such that you prove with all the instrument which is called "entromissoire", of which the form comes hereafter, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, so let it go through above for a long time.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, do not leave any skin that contains that moisture, for it will return immediately if you leave anything. 
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; 
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; 
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And do this as often as needed for a night. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	Then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you are sure that it no longer remains at night;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds a lot of fat, then do this according to this form for a long time. 
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	And you should rub in ointments and scrape it from all sides, and apply all your healing milk for the boil where it lies. 
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the artery goes against you, do what I told you afterwards. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same for an abscess if it is ripe, and for the waist and for curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the abscess pierces it and draws out moisture, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses or boils have no moisture, and like those were the boils that I cut from an old woman's head. 
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	And I found the boil as hard as a stone, rough and white, and it could not break.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if one had cut into it, they would have done just as much harm as cutting into a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming or appearing, especially those that come at the head of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be made in the lowest place so that the pus can come out.  
et les cure si com il covient.	And the cure should be done as it is appropriate. 
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come in other parts of the body, and they are very painful, and they are joined together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its own rib, just as the wart and the abscess on the head, as we have said;  
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and there are many resemblances to these scrofula.  
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some which contain moisture, and some which are malignant and will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In that one then which you see of good disposition to touch, and resembles the color of the body, and moves at each point and is not adherent to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the duct, and is not deep;  
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	it is fitting that you cut it from above and scrape it at each point, and extend the two lips of the wound to the sutures, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses on the head; 
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and do not let the instrument be too sharp nor cutting, lest the hands slip, and do not press too hard before, lest you cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut a vein or artery and it will not let you work, put powdered vitriol into the wound, or some powders that staunch blood, and remove the plague; 
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood has stopped, return to your work until you complete it; 
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then inquire with your index finger whether any small scrofula remain, if so, cut and cleanse them.  
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if it has a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not fitting that you cut that scrofula at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself without harm. 
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the wound with old cotton steeped in Egyptian ointment, then dress it.  
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out all the scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you know how to cut off its root, and draw with force, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofula that hold superfluity, pierce them where it appears dead; 
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce it as the one mentioned before, in dependence, then apply bandages with ointment and such things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption. 
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is well cleansed, apply a dressing with ointment containing charcoal, until it is healed. 
de squinance	from squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and that is the writing of their words. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have strabismus, it is necessary that the slit in the throat which is called "epiglottis" be scraped. 
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And one should not do this, for all the veins and the lung of the patient are affected in those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the tonsils. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the windpipe of the throat, it is fitting to lift the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary then, when we wish to split the epiglottis, that we split it below three circles or four, a small slit across, between the two circles, or according to the quantity of the slit of the face, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those things are suitable for the section of the epiglottis if there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from it. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to the whole length, then splits the heart as far as it comes to the chin.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut out the bone marrow, as we have said. 
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section through which the phlegm of the chest passes out, and by the defect of the voice. 
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed in which strangulation is doubtful, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart, and sew it all up without touching the cartilage. 
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that promote flesh growth, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is all torn open and the patient is judged dead, and the defect is in the pharynx.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut out the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death. 
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And because the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease had passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and clean it, until it was healed. 
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I have seen. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels from her windpipe; 
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to treat her, and I found her as if dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found blood coming from it; although it had not pierced a vein nor gone farther than the throat, the veins were ruptured by the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated her until she was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it only happened to the young woman that her voice became hoarse, and afterwards returned to its normal state; 
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for this reason I say that you should not fear cutting the epiglottis. 
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of yellow, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it occurs in two ways: 
naturez, et accidens;	Nature and accidents; 
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Or nature has no part. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And accidents are according to two manners, one of which resembles fat to us, and the other manner resembles an abscess which comes from our arteries; 
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear, and it is not fitting to work with hot iron except in that which is small, and he tests and searches at all the entrances.  
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as we find our fat, and it cannot go through any vein, then cut it off as we cut off the warts, and treat all its top, if there is any.  
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And surround it well soon, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed. 
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many manners of ours, of which I will say all the resemblances;  
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and therefore it is necessary that I say all the difference which is between us and issue. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that issue is heat and fever lasting, as long as the boilings are passed, and rot is accomplished; 
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then rest the fever and the heat.  
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With new there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains its own juice, which is its own bag and is according to the color of the body, and begins also as a pea, and grows large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two resemblances, either greasy or moist, and many of the colors are as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a wound, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument which is called "entromissoire," according to its shape or chapter which is afterwards.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of the inquisition of abscesses for us is that you take or a more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers, little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the heart, then that it be according to the size of the abscess; 
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the instrument, and take care that it does not leap out. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs clear, whatever its color, then do as I have said for the other abscesses; 
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the instrument no moisture comes, know that it is fatty; then do as I have said in a cross shape, and take hold with pincers, and lightly scratch it on each side and guard the garment where it lies so that you draw it clean with the needle.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it out clean, then do so in pieces so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the pain will return many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if even a small piece remains and it does not bother you, then apply the wound with some corrosive sharp powders, and extract the wound, and put soothing things on the hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is large, sew the two lips of the wound, and treat it with what causes flesh to grow. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein beats against you or another thing hastens and apply powdered vitriol, and let it rest for two days or three, as long as the wound ripens, and stills the boiling of blood; 
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to covering what has remained dry. 
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of inserting instruments, and they are of three kinds: 
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three kinds: 
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistulas; 
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like needles with which we sew charms, and they are made of citric iron, or of iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are the best, and are more proven for black pitch to surround the curves of a fistula. 
et sont de III manieres:	And they are of three kinds:  
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the opening. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the needles are of many resemblances, as you see here: 
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small; 
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are needles that have two curves in three ways also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and there are needles that have three curves, and they are also of three ways; 
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and there are needles that have two curves, and needles with only one curve, and they are of three ways also; 
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And all this is necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these is what we make are cutting, and some of them do not cut more than one side, from which we flay the veins, for this we do not cut the vein nor the nerve; 
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these inserters are the alamel replied in handles, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses; 
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:  
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and we do not use them more than in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and at no time do we make another small instrument resembling punches of fists, according to this form, with which we staunch blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it back in place so that it heals properly in accordance with the veins and arteries, and never again return to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, so much that they resemble women's breasts; 
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to heal them, if it is necessary, should follow the form of these lines b. up to g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine made into a paste, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; 
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast hangs down, and is softened by its size as it happens with women, then make two cuts on it, by two similar incisions;  
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is connected to the other at the end of one and the beginning of the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from line b. up to line g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then flay the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed. 
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of bleeding, then you must fill the wound with softened cotton in corrosive ointment. 
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it until it softens the remaining and fat, then treat it until it is healed.  
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses which come under the armpits are types of hard scrofula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those which contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g.:
