Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then dress the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, make it as we said for incisions of scrofula, and if the wound closes inwards, apply a cautery as we said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is severed and the skin above it is sewn together, many times abscesses come about, and the same thing happens to a swollen vein and an abscess. 
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if the knower knows when it is for the artery, the abscess is long and perfect. 
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it at your fingertips, if you feel dislocation; 
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, it must be put back in its place.  
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cut this abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and at the angles or neck and many other places, and it is very large. 
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to avoid the use of iron, and he who is in charge must also avoid it, and in the one who is swollen from an artery making its way through the skin for a long time; 
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then operate with lancets and cleanly separate the artery from the tissues, until it is exposed;  
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then put a needle underneath it and make it pierce through to the other side, and remove the artery with a doubled thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; 
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then press the place between the two strands of a speculum until the pus that is in it comes out, and let the abscess be released. 
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply a bandage that compresses the wound, as long as the ligaments tighten. 
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with an ointment suitable for this, until it is healed. 
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is as large as a vein, it is fitting that you hold in your hand what you can take from the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand and make it pierce, and let there be a double thread so that you pull it from the other side;  
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie the abscess, as I have told you, with a ligature from one of the two sides to the two ends of the thread. 
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the thread will come out, put another needle all along the thread below all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull out the threads in four places; 
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut the excess of the heart and leave that which is tied; 
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put a cloth moistened in wine and oil on top of it, then apply dressings of tents and ointments until it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in arteries and veins, abscesses come to nerves when they are strained, or through too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens most often in the shoulders and hips and in all places where there are joints, and it is a pain of abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in several positions without pain; 
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is extracted, the patient feels pain, and it is not in perfect position with the body, but under the heart; 
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and move well on all sides, and do not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and the one that is in joints should not be covered by iron. 
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	lest it cause contraction; 
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the one that is on the head or forehead, make the skin with a spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscesses are small, if you have some tweezers, and cover it at its root; 
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if you suspend it to the lancet, and flay it, then bone and assemble the wound with stitches, and heal it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of large ulcers hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes it occurs in bellies and not elsewhere, a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and the root is subtle, and the head large; 
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are some small and some very large; 
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw a man who had two or three things on his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had small roots, and they were easily cut open, and moisture constantly flowed from them. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them off and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six ounces. The work of cutting is such that if you look and see that the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist and has fine roots; 
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if the cut is made with a broad spatula, and you have a fire cautery present. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For at the waist there often come excessive flows of blood, and if your patient faints, then hasten to cauterize; 
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient fainting and afraid of the incision with iron, then take a good thread of flax, and tie the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; 
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease to pull the thread of flax until it reaches the joint, and passes through it by its effort. 
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are thick, it is painful to cut them directly through the abdomen, but you can well cut half of them, and then cauterize them so they do not grow back. 
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then dress the wound, and be careful not to cut the tendon which is of a dark color and poor sense and full of milk. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the arm is strong
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a boil comes from cautery of a wound or an incision, and it is on the belly and in some of the bowels, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before it, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from a rupture of the intestine and through an opening in the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens from various exits. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its hips if it responds, and then returns, and by chance if it is squeezed, and increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and through great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and opens well when you press it with your hand, but do not constrain it. 
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs: the abscess is large and hard, and it is fixed according to a certain quantity. 
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must let the healing take place.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the bowels, it is fitting that you instruct the patient to hold his breath and be stretched out straight, then bind all around the arm.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then command him to grasp often between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed with all of the spatula, then extend half of the abscess above to all the great one. 
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then bind the limb with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk tightly, and let the knot be loose. 
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then work on half of the abscess extended over the bandage, and push your index finger in, and squeeze the intestines. 
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught under the bandage, untie it, and push the intestine out of the belly cavity. 
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find pus, take it with your thumb nail, and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if an artery or vein opposes you, wind it carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, put them with two threads, and insert the two needles around what you have done in a cross shape so that you pierce. 
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess into four parts on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and let the wound remain until it dries, and let the dead flesh come off by itself. 
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	where you find it subtle and rotten, then treat it as necessary, and drain the abscess as we have said; 
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as necessary, and suture the area. 
dou chancre	a sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division the likenesses of ulcers, and how one must work with medicine, and how one must avoid treatment with iron;
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and say that the ulcer spreads in the marrow, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and they say that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be scraped away like an ulcer that is on the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, one should remove it all when it is at the beginning; 
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, you must not approach it, for I have never been able to heal any. 
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	No one heals without me before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the works, when it is in place or we can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile sometimes. 
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	Then make him fast if he has manifest repletion, then put the patient in a good place to do the work; 
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	Then gird your tunic or shirt and shave his head from all sides and all bones leaving nothing. 
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And let the blood run freely and wipe the place with your hand or some other thing, and if the flow of blood goes against the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it with another cure until it is healed. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy and in what manner the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure which is made by medicine and that which is cured by iron. 
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only split; 
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one must not touch it with iron in these two ways: 
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and yposarche, for they are deadly things; 
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore, when you treat this kind of dropsy which is called “split” and the treatment does not work, consider whether the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the bowels and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt; 
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient is of strong constitution, and he has no other illness besides dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must work thus: 
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Lay the patient straight upon your hands, and have your assistant press on the belly at the lowest part below the breastbone, then take the sharpest pointed spatula according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp on two sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	At a point, but it should not be so inserted that it can reach the intestines when put in, and it cannot be bleached. 
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	Then look to see if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines:  
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	If it is necessary, you should cut into them below the shoulder blade three fingers' width to the right. 
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	And if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be on the left side of the shoulder blade three fingers' width. 
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	And if it is due to the spleen, it should be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie upon the incision so that the superfluities do not run into the weak part.  
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument and push it in, lift your hand as far as possible between the skin and the muscle, just like when flaying to the amount of a fingernail or so.  
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to the eighth place, and this is the place of the needle, then pull hard, and push this instrument which has this form: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it resembles a subtle silver cane, and is made of willow or artichoke wood light, and has a small hole at the bottom part. 
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	And on one side, there are three holes. 
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	And two on the other side, and one on another.  
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision which the scribes use to cut the feather: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	At the head above is the point so that when the instrument comes to the needle's eye, it descends now onto the instrument.  
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	Empty then half or a third part, for if you empty more than is needed at that hour, the patient might die by chance due to the spirit's release from the weapon, or the head weakens, or he approaches death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to the void of its virtue, and according to what the disposition of the patient's virtue signifies; and his pulse. 
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is now held for the heart which stops the opening that is above the face, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; 
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and treat the point with a small amount; 
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this every day, and be careful not to press while it remains but a prick of a point. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt the patient, and you leave a lot of point, if the cure is from burial or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and if he drinks; 
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the treatment of drying medicines until it is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the sharp object, as I said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	from the removal of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who do not have a hole in their penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary as soon as possible, he has not pierced with a very subtle instrument according to this form.
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put or make a small plug of lead, and tie it and hold it for III days or IIII and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug, and urinate, and then put it back; 
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance none is needed, for the urine that comes out will not leave it closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose anus is small, if it is treated with a plum stone as we have said, it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the opening in their place are unfortunate, for no one is born who has the opening at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis up; 
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the end, and it is a bad disease.  
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on his back, then extend the head of the penis and the foreskin as thin as a feather, so that the hole pierces in the middle, as it should. 
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful of the flow of blood which often comes, and if it happens, let it be stemmed by one who stems blood, and dress the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Often these abscesses come on the penis, and are a sight of foul flesh; 
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are malignant and non-malignant ones;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	it is fitting that you take them with a subtle lancet, and cut and cleanse all of them, then put softened cotton with Egyptian ointment on them; 
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it with diachylon ointment until it is healed.  
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the pus is malignant, of a foul color and corrupting, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have grasped it, and if the foreskin is on top of the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the foreskin which is inside first.  
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when it is joined, then let the wound heal outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat it together, unless the head of the penis is very secure so that it is not pierced, then blackness and corruption will come to its penis and testicles. 
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to cut away everything that is black and corrupted, then bind on a plaster of honey and flour which is made from the bark of pomegranates and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bloodletting is required, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	Cauteries help in two ways together: 
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, in the stopping of blood and in the corruption.  
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you bring or conduct a cane of lead to the penis, and the patient urinates among it. 
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the hairs grow around the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or an abscess, it is necessary that you scrape it with a sharp instrument, until the bonds are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; 
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a grievous thing to do this, it is necessary that you scrape it with a spatula any spot on the head of the penis and of the skin; 
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then you must carefully separate them both, and put a fine linen cloth softened in cold water so that it does not burn at the beginning. 
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a breaking of continuity like other wounds; 
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Whenever we do this work of our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the lightest for safety. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I want most masters and surgeons who performed circumcisions used a knife, with force, and a whole scalpel; 
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	which would cause the heart to faint because there are two layers, and by chance if one cuts above and leaves the one below. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Here it is necessary to cut again, and the pain is doubled, and at the cleansing which is done with two layers, the point of the member is not well secured.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and in the cleansing of the ulcer if the iron should happen to escape and spoil the work, and many times they are born without needing cleansing and I want it so. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Regarding modification which is made to the strength of all the thread I have found the goodness of experience, for the strengths cut precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut equally in a straight line all at once;  
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but let the threads be well twisted around the leather; 
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if they understand, that you are only doing to tie the thread around the penis, and then let them rejoice in all the ways that you can;  
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then make it come out straight between your hands, and support its weight between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; 
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then put your hand on the penis and blow or breathe on it, and pull it upward until the head of the penis is inside; 
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then cleanse it well of the filth that has gathered there, then bind the place with a doubled thread, then bind it below the spot to the other binding; 
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	And hold it with your two hands by the second binding to the thumb and index finger, and tie between the two bindings, then lift the core on top quickly and treat the head of the penis; 
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	Then let the blood run drop by drop, for that is best;  
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put powder on top and on top of the powder a dressing made from a half-cooked egg yolk tempered with rose water, confected with good fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of forces for cleansing is this:  
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The two jaws should be held and sharp, and the jaws should also be as large as the handle evenly: 
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of purification is when the kernels inside escape at the incision; 
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your fingernail, so that the pus will form an abscess; 
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	And the tip similarly, and if you cannot hold it to your fingernail, then use tweezers and then the tip. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if it passes three days and what is below the penis is swollen, leave it until the abscess under it is appeased, and scrape it lightly. 
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If you can move the tip, and keep yourself away from the penis, it will not harm anything.  
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Treat then the place of these internal wounds with powder, as we have said in our treatise on powders, and if the tip goes beyond the kernels too much and it rises above, it will not harm. 
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it as we have said until it is healed. 
dou retenement de l’urine	For the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to a stone, or congealed blood, or bowel obstruction, or a new growth, or similar things as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to a stone in the bladder neck, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent on their knees. 
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	And let their feet be placed on the back and extend their belly above the back and restrain the patient from moving as much as they can.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And then the neck of the bladder is compressed for the expulsion of the stone above so that the urine is released. 
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it does not come as we have said and the patient feels great pain then you must administer extraction with an instrument called a "syringe" which has this form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let it be of refined silver, light as a bird's feather; 
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let the handle be a palm and a half long, and refined at the head. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of drawing out urine is that you take a doubled thread, and tie at the head a piece of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; 
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the excess wool and put it just to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and make the patient sit on a seat, and anoint his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water;  
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the thigh; 
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then insert the syringe forward until the bladder, and feel the patient come to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless because the one who guides where it goes is crooked; 
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then stretch the thread all along the wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and let the urine run. 
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And begin the syringe again until the bladder is emptied, and align the patient.  
des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scaldings or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see sharp waters and medicines distilled, then make all the instrument which is called a "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: 
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see;  
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and let the veins be cut so that the medicine flows well into the penis without addition, if one can draw out the moisture, and insert when needed. 
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	And when you see your medicines enter the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and draw with the one that is inside.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you treat the moisture at the caster, and then firmly reset the traction. 
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	If the moisture enters in, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; 
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	And this is the form of a subtle clyster with which one clysters the bladder: 
si est ci:	This is it: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or of boxwood, and its head is higher;  
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below at its side where the linen strings are attached; 
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	Then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture which you have seen used to clyster the bladder, then tie it between the two sides with a good strong double thread, and heat that part of the moisture over the fire; 
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Then put the head of the clyster into the urethra, then hold your hand on the bladder with all the moisture flowing in, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; 
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle out of it, and pierce it round about. 
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	Then put a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dish, and put in it what you see of oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it to the instrument. 
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said in the division the ways of stone and the extraction together with medicines; 
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and we have said the difference between a stone lodged in the reins and all the signs, and what kind of stone one should work on with an incision.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis; 
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the sharp point of the stone resembles a sharp spike in its thinness. 
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	And it opens wide, and grasps the patient's penis, and bends it many times, then twists it.  
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	And many of these points are embedded. 
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	And the healing is easy for children until they are four years old, and it is very painful for the elderly, and it is in between for those who are between youth and old age. 
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	And the treatment is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the phlegm that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet and push him down and move him below so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and comes out sometimes from above.  
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then make him sit between your hands evenly, and his hands be under his thighs so that the bladder is entirely inclined downward; 
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then take hold of it and touch it inside. 
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut upon the stone.  
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not move at all when touched, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand if the patient is a woman, or your middle finger if the patient is a young man; 
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and insert it into their fundament and grasp the stone, and when you feel it on your finger then pull it to the neck of the bladder. 
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press upon your finger, and push it out where you see that you should cut.  
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the assistant to press upon the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the testicles in the part where the incision is made. 
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then he puts the spatula in a cutting shape. 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And it cuts between what is between the buttocks and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock. 
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And it is straight on the stone, and your two fists should be right at the fundament, and the waist should be wide externally and narrow internally, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large. 
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	If by chance the press is at the two fists which are at the fundament, so that it jumps out without effort.
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	And know that there are stones with angles and edges.  
si est griés a issir;	If it is grated to come out. 
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And if there are some that are underneath, resembling a bullet and round, of which the exit is easy.  
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Therefore, for those which have angles and edges, make the incision larger. 
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not jump, it is fitting that you extract it with tongs which are also like a file at the head, in order to pull out the stone so that it does not escape. 
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you insert beneath it a subtle instrument bent at the head; 
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot bring it out this way, enlarge the hole a little, and if the sinew is cut, extract it with vitriol. 
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And if there are more than one stone, insert the largest first into the neck of the bladder, then one above it, and then another, and so on with the smaller ones if there are several. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be sewn and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	either he dies, or his urine comes forth immediately because the veins cannot solder together. 
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nonetheless, exert yourself to draw it out, or to break it up with tongs, as long as you draw it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and extract it, and put on top a soft cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess. 
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then let the patient rest on his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.  
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if it arises very well in the place of oil and water, then treat it with diaphycon ointment and basil ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if abscesses come to the wound and corrode it, and there are blood clots in the bladder, and urine is retained by this, which is known in part that it does not flow out with the urine: 
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Then put your finger in the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help it in all ways that you know, until it is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that every hour when you treat it, you bind his two thighs together, and apply the medicines to the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is lodged in the urethra and stuck there, and the urine cannot pass; 
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if the treatment that I have described thus far is followed, you are excused from a surgical incision by this treatment. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already done this myself.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron shaped like this, with three prongs fixed on a fire.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it cannot move back into the bladder; 
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then gently insert the instrument into the penis until it reaches the stone;  
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the instrument in your hand against the stone bit by bit until you can pierce the stone through to the other side; 
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the penis.  
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is broken soon, and jumps out with urine, and is carried away by the patient; 
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	And if you cannot do this for anything that defends it, then tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then make a rod at the place of the stone between the two ties, then pull it out, untie the tie, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cure it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It sometimes happens that a stone is lodged in women, and if it ever does happen, the cure is painful and forbidden for three reasons: 
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	One is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	And the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to uncover herself at her privy parts, even when she is chaste. 
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third way is if by chance one cannot find a woman who is well-versed in this art of hands; 
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is more deeply embedded than the stone of man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessity compels you to do this, it is fitting that you take a midwife who is well-knowing, and she is rarely found; and if you cannot find her, then you should not hesitate to use a small, subtle knife. 
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and present a wise midwife in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command her from the inquiry of the stone;  
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very well if the woman is a virgin: 
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is fitting for her to put her finger or foundation and seek the stone;  
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, if she compresses it below her finger, and recommends that she put her finger where the patient is, and wants and presses her left hand on the bladder. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, it is fitting that she moves it quickly from the entrance of the bladder to below, as far as it comes to the root of the thigh; 
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then press on the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the bone, where it is moved and appears, and feels the stone in that part;  
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and does not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the size be small at first; 
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then put the knife in the size, if you feel the stone so enlarge the wound as much as the stone can come out forcefully, and know that many kinds of stones are: 
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	This is to know, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have points. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the resemblances to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the flesh swells, apply powdered vitriol to it, and hold it for an hour until the flesh is cauterized. 
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	Then return to your work, as long as the stone is hard, and have instruments that I have told you about for extracting stones from men to help you in your work. 
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	And if the flesh swells, and it is from an artery that has been severed, apply the powder to the area and bind it with tents and bandages, and do not restart this work, and leave the stone and do not remove it, lest the patient should die.
puis cure la plaie.	Then treat the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the swelling subsides, you return to your work, as long as the stone remains.
de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Ramic aquose is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white phlegm, which is located below the heart of the testicles, which contains the seed. 
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	And it is called "phlegm", and at no time is it properly in the fabric of the seed, if one thinks that it is another seed. 
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	And this is the skin of the testicle between the white phlegm which we have said;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	And this would not have occurred otherwise. 
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice comes from weakness which comes to the yolks, and is spread out this matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And at no time if there is percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors:  
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	Either it is a color tending toward yellow, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to recognize this collection, for if it is white as we have said, then the abscess has returned. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the fabric itself, then the abscess will return with part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought to be another egg. 
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	And if the moisture is between the leather of the testicles and the white membrane, then one feels it well. 
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	Therefore, when you see the color of the moisture, test all the instruments, of which the shape is described above. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, which comes after the introducer, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cauterize it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be purged according to our power and the repletion of his body. 
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	Then place him on his back, on something a foot high, and put many cloths under him. 
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	Then sit on his left side and instruct the assistant to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the testicles.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the scalpel, sharp and clean, and cut through the skin of the testicles among them lengthwise, right down to the point, and make your incision straight, parting the skin of the testicles until you see white flesh, and carefully scrape it according to its nature.  
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the white flesh plainly with a sharp needle, make one large opening and extract all the fluid, then apply your ointments and bandage the wound upward. 
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	And do not touch the heart of the testicles, but only the white flesh.  
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Cut all or in pieces immediately the side of it subtly, so that if you do not cut it wisely, the fluid will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the egg jumps out of your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the sinew. 
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then bring together the two leaves of the heart of the onions with a suture, then treat it as you would other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, in order to stop the flow of blood; 
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then cut the onion at all its suspensions and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.  
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the point is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; 
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	if you cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound linen moistened in rose oil; 
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put damp wool soaked in wine and oil on the two joints 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths and make them of tow according to this likeness and let them be joined together by stitching at the throat of the breeches, and one of the ends take upon the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the hilt; 
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two chiefs upon the two angles, and let all be assembled together in the loop of the breeches;  
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And it is often medicine this branch of the cautery in place of a blade of iron, and it is that you take a subtle culinary cautery knife, and cut the skin of the testicles, and let it be heated as we have said so that the white fascia that contains the point is uncovered; 
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take the cautery according to this form and pierce that fascia with awls, and flay it with this subtle hot cautery;  
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And loosen the cautery in every way you can until you completely remove it. 
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	And be careful that the fire does not touch the eye.  
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	And know that this work is safer 
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and easier to manage in terms of blood loss and less dangerous than operations.  
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if anything goes wrong, whether it's an abscess forming, bleeding, or something else, treat what is causing the problem according to what has already been said. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure because of its horror, then perform a perforation as I have told you, and only when you are sure by the signs we have mentioned that the aqueous humor is gone, make the patient sit on a raised seat. 
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	Then pierce the abscess at the bottom part of it, wide enough for the whole spatula to fit, and make the incision as long as the body.  
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the opening be wide so that all the sharp point may pass through 
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the spot and bind it and let it run through the remaining point then treat it until the wound is healed 
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not let the point out in the mouth of the wound then it is necessary that you put a quill or an instrument with which one treats the points of hydropsy in it, of which the shape is described above
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the sore and know that the point will return and will gather after six months or thereabouts and when it is gathered as before then the patient will spend his days like that  
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this branch there are more dangers
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the resemblances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say therefore that many abscesses come on the body, and likewise on the testicles; 
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is by many cases. 
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by excessive sour and hot acidity, which is spread to the testicles, or by percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; 
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and there is no pain found, and it is an abscess sorrow;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance there are some abscesses gray porous and piercing, and of purple color, and sometimes it comes from a new artery, or from swelling of the vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a new artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers; 
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it is not right that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	He who is made of swelling of the vein is known by his arrangement at the touch of the fingers, and one can well make the incision on this resemblance, and on the other humors; 
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	And when you cut the heart of the testicles, then lift the egg up high, and the vein from the white sinew, and deliver the suspensory ligament from all sides of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already dead with these humors, then it is necessary that you draw out the egg, and cut it. 
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is air in the sinew, or in those that are within the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that tension, and cut the heart roundly. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is behind or further back, it is necessary that you cut all of it and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling the bud, with softening of the testicles, and he who is ill groans when he goes. 
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And the treatment of this disease is just as perilous as the one before it, and nonetheless we will tell you its work, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then you put the suspensory of the testicles below your thighs, at all the vessels which are near the penis, and grasp the masters, and extend them. 
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then cut with a sharp scalpel at a distance from the vessels so that they are uncovered, and then flay on each side as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples. 
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then he puts in a needle with a doubled thread and ties it at the first place where the vein appeared, and ties it straight to the other end. 
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then he cuts them in half straight according to the length of the body, and removes the corrupted humors. 
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then treat the wound as you would any other where you are drawing out the poison so that no vessel breaks and nourishes one of the boils. 
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	For if this does not happen, and all the vessels are visible, then you must drain the boils of all the vessels. 
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	So that the bone does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped. 
de la routure dou syfac	Of a broken bone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrence of this rupture is by the section that comes or arises on the belly in the part of the intestines, so the intestines descend from that break to one of the boils. 
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	And this rupture is either at the syfac or from the stretching of it, and these two manners come from many causes. 
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	either from percussion, or from a jump, or from a blow, or from lifting a heavy weight, and by similar things. 
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is a stretching of the sinews, if it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; 
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal towards the end, because the sinew presses on the intestine. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a section of the sciatic nerve, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and there are diverse abscesses appearing beneath the skin nearby, and this is due to the exit of the intestine and the body's rejection of the sciatic nerve.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never detach the intestines with the entrails, and they are retained within, and cause great pain to suffer to the patient, especially when it is pressed.
