ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or that are made according to their locations in the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck or head or foot or belly or liver and similar limbs; 
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the treatment of each wound and begin with simple head wounds because remembrance will come in its chapter.  
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, if you take care if it is from a striking of a stone or similar things and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt a hot abscess: 
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if it bleeds quickly from the cephalic vein itself, if only a little blood comes from the wound, and it is bled from the opposite side of the injured part 
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid having the patient overeat wine and rich foods. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it does not want to bleed, let its meat be reduced, and do not drink wine, nor eat any pork. 
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if a pustule should come, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine. 
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no hot pustule, put on the wound, if it is fresh and bleeds freely, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will say a little later. 
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved it, put on some ointments until it is healed.  
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by stitching, then bring them together with sutures as I will say for abdominal wounds, from stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is uncovered from the bone, and it can, and does not hold but to one point, then stitch it. 
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then treat the wound with medicine and restore hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotten leather, and it does not reach the bone, stitch all the rot together, then cut it away, then treat it. 
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if it has an artery in the wound or vein which without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then cauterize the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread. 
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, then cauterize it.  
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: 
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and put this powder on it so that it fuses as if the fire had moved it. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is: 
pren encens une partie;	Take incense one part; 
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts; 
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	quicklime three parts, and powder it finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it burns well and joins with all its blood;  
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind it well, and leave it unbound, if it does not swell; 
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do this with chalk alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the fire has dried the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has already moved the wound, do not put this powder on it at all;  
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put some digested ointments on it, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it flows freely; 
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure of other cures until he is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with subtle pincers; 
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves in the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the treatment alone and not apply anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be underneath, such as chamomile boiled in fresh water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber also boiled in fresh water, and other stones of alum according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is covered and full of pus, then pierce it lower. 
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut and blood flows from it, then tie it off, bind it, and cautery is necessary. 
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is preserved through which the flesh goes, sew the heart onto the bone of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape. 
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then remove it carefully and leave it for a few days, then treat it with dry dressings until it is healed. 
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then scrape it.  
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And if there are bone fragments, remove them all if you can. If those that you cannot reach, then leave them until the wound has suppurated and is cleansed and the way out is cleared.  
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, put powder on top of the powder that I have mentioned. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a cut from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if the wound lets out wind, while the patient is standing. 
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	You should then know that the wound is mortal; 
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep and is fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it because of the blood that will not stop flowing completely and return to the heart and kill the patient. 
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	But apply a drawing ointment, and bind it twice a day; 
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to soak up excess moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.  
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if there will come no spasm, nor evil tremor of heart nor twitchings of the flesh; 
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	So cure it then with bandages and other treatments, until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and the work, then know that there is a fistula;  
si la cure si com on doit.	if the care is as one must. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision and it is simple, whether on the thigh or back, care for that which is in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, with sutures; 
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder, and if it is driven into the bone, and has split into pieces, clean the wound, and treat the wounds if they are detached; 
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not removed, let the wound fester, so it will make extraction easier. 
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds of other limbs, judgement is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	regarding rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude, by which entry of others is permitted.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because one puts the intestines back in more carefully if they are not put back hot.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell quickly when they feel cold, and do not go back in carefully, and therefore a moderate wound is better, because one can move the intestines to their place more easily than the others.  
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that a rupture of the belly is according to four manners: 
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body, and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds. 
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And nevertheless they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it.  
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is out, and grievous thing is to put it back in, this is by one of two manners: 
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen because of the cold.  
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in two ways: 
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in warm water only, or you cook in warm water, vinegar and cypress and spikenard, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And at no time make this wine restraining, and it is a mother that has only one breast to reduce swelling. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestines with sharp or sweet and well-cooked herbs, for by this is aligned the entry to few things. 
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	And if it cannot enter, make a small cut at the instrument with which we cut hemorrhoids. 
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	And the first remedy is a mother that is smaller than the waist, so that none should be carved without great necessity. 
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And these are the instruments for splitting it: 
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If you cut inside the curvature and don't tear, and see here the shape:  
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude, if you can put them back into their natural form in their proper place, do so, for this is worth much.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower part of the belly, it is fitting that you make the patient lie on his back, and place his legs higher than his head. 
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and the breast higher than the parts below, and also if the break in the belly is in one of the two parts, then put your understanding so that the injured part is higher than the other. 
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is fitting to administer what I say in large and small wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds, put what appears to you, then have between your hands one minister who holds all the break with his hand and brings together the lips; 
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common way of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound a space of two fingers, and put in a needle where it has a good strong thread; 
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the sinew, which is below the skin inside, as far as you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the two edges of the sinew four together;  
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then strain a double thread onto the needle in two parts, then join the two edges of the wound carefully together and leave one finger space. Then insert another needle. 
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the thread as you did with the first needle and do not cease doing this according to how many needles are needed until the whole wound is closed. 
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be medium sized, between thin and thick, because thin needles pierce all the flesh and too thick ones cannot enter well. 
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore it is necessary that they are medium sized; 
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	And it is not right to push the needles too far through the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open the wound before the stitching.  
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	And then cut the threads of the needles so they do not bother the patient while sleeping and put bandages or cloths over the needle threads to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed. 
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for it suffices one needle or two. 
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and it consists of assembling the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the sinew together on one needle with a strong medium thread. 
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you have pierced all these sides together, pull the needle back to where you began, in the manner one sews cloth. 
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	And place a distance between each stitch the thickness of a small fingernail.  
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch heals a man, and I sewed a wound one had on his belly or chest which was inflicted with a knife, and the wound was more than a handspan large, and the intestines protruded two handspans, and the wound lay in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back his intestines after they had been outside for XXIV hours, and the wound was sutured up to XV days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they thought he would die, and it was a miracle. 
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not anoint him at all, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine. 
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: 
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and push it from the outer part to the inner part. 
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the flesh straight through, take the thread or twine or whatever you used to push the needle through and make it pierce from the other side, from the inner part to the outer part. 
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as furriers sew furs, and that you leave one time the thread on one side and take it up on the other, until the whole stitch is complete. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of suturing, which Galen properly calls, is as some do, who bring the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the heads of the thread to the other head, in this manner: 
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert a needle or head of silk thread close by, and pierce only that spot, and leave the two heads of the thread. 
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and pierce it from the part behind to that inside, with the two heads of the thread. 
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce one and the other from the part behind to that inside, with two other heads of silk thread which are on the other side. 
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the gentler manner of suturing and the more common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen said this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, or he has thread in each. 
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew straps; 
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is halfway down the belly, the stitching is more painful than in other places of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: 
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the fire had moved it, then put back together the intestine, and the seam;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on burnt charcoal powder, and if the fire has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound swells; 
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and sew the thread, and let the sinews be joined together, and the muscle fibers
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed; 
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you do not have medicine, put upon it as soon as it begins to fester, old cotton and move it twice a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you need no other medicine in many situations unless the wounds are complex; 
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound will cause infection to the principal limbs, it is fitting that you moisten linen lightly in tempered oil or rose oil and place it around the edges and under the armpits. 
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if he feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, give enemas of warm red wine and likewise if the putrefaction comes up to the intestines.  
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce it within and know that when it is the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the plantations of veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the gristle jumps from the wound, put it back as you would the intestine, while it is fresh; 
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and has become green or black, you must bind the black area so that blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries. 
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut what is between the ligatures and put the two ends hanging down from the part below the wound until it comes out to align the extraction when the gristle shrinks and the wound swells. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the fracture of the bone
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, you can restore it in some men, for I have seen a man who was wounded in the belly by a spear; 
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and excrement and wind came out.  
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put a remedy according to what I could, and did not cease to refine it until he was healed, and his wounds closed. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw his wounds close, I doubted that the patient would not have pain in his belly; 
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he did not have any pain, but remained in better health, and ate and drank;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in a certain way: 
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take thread with large heads, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it squeezes its mouth shut; 
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut the thread head, and it will stay so that it cannot loosen, then put another thread afterwards in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed;
et cout la plaie.	And sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If those hairs burn inside the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: 
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the end of this thread from the intestine, which is well-detached, and then tie to the end of this thread a fine linen thread twisted tightly, then pass the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, and straighten it at the break; 
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of suturing is nothing more than according to the way of cunning and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal folds, there is nothing but subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it grows old, is called universally "fistula," and the same when it is healed and drawn inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	A fistula is, according to the green color, a hard and white node, where there is no pain felt, and it is also raised like the feather of a bird; 
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And sometimes the bowels are clear, and other times thick; 
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes it's few, and other times enough; 
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	And as I have spoken of in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only due to one of nine causes: 
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	That is to say, by the smallness of blood or flesh; 
ou por sa malice;	or because of its malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and on the edges that does not allow new flesh to grow; 
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there are too many bowels;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the wound is purulent and the matter is of poor quality; 
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good for healing;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is in the manner of a pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where by its nature digestion is delayed in the region, and feeling is slow, and it swells; 
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:  
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it is necessary for me to teach you the treatment of a fistula which is made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all the members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the face, or the intestines, or the bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; 
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it extends to the nature of the principal member, and similar ones.  
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are of this kind are due to poor healing, and there is nothing but toil, and ignorance; 
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not come all the way to the place I have mentioned, and you are confident of the cure and see it clearly, then take a tent of linen or iron, if the fistula is straight; 
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, if it searches with a subtle attempt to plumb, for the plummet bends and moves around the twistiness; 
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it with probes, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for the moisture will pass from one opening to another and cleanse it; 
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then let the patient bleed as much as you can, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is raised in a proper manner, and inquire well of the patient about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it; 
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the corruption and rotten flesh that are within;  
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure as long as it is healed, and if the fistula is deep in the right place, it is fitting that you cut it thoroughly, as much as you can, then put tents softened in medicine water, and push them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity which remains at the bottom; 
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put ointments spreading healthy flesh, as long as it is healed; 
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves trouble you or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then wash it as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then treat it with spreading healthy flesh things as long as it is healed; 
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healed, and goes back in as before, know that you have not gone far enough. 
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if you uncover and scrape as much as you can until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore it to its place; 
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, it is good. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it; 
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature; 
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small bone corrupted and you can pull it out with forceps, extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, remove them all, leaving none behind; 
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture works against you and there is no error or fear, cut away the moisture and flesh and free the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something promoting decay on the wound, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then you will be able to remove the bones more easily. 
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it is a large bone, such as those of the leg or thigh, only allow the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound. 
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is a large part that has become corrupt and comes up to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	you must sew and cover everything up to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take an example and help in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause, so that the matter came to his leg and it swelled into a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it.  
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the sick through their folly worked so much on the abscesses that they opened them and corroded many substances and became fistulas and there came many openings which all flowed with pus and moisture from the body. 
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And many sick people put treatment on for two years and there was no wise man in the art of hands until I was called upon and saw his leg and the medicines by which he was treated and what flowed from the openings with great force. 
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And it became red the flesh of the youth and had a yellow color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pushed a tent into one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that some came against each other from all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hurried then and dug into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came even to the bone within. 
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I cut away all that appeared to me of the corrupted bone and thought there was no other corruption except for that which I removed. 
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And begin to restore the wound with hot medicines for a long time, and it cannot heal. 
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And then I began again and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I treated it, and then I removed it, and I tried to heal the place. 
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	But I could not do so until I scraped away a palm's width of bone, and the wound pulsed throughout its entire length, then I restored it with medicines. 
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it healed and closed quickly, and I did not have to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation it often bled, but it was healed completely, and in place of the bone there grew a hard flesh, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contrariety at all, neither in coming nor in going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place in the body, it must be treated in this way: 
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take linen and bind it to the head of the bone that is visible, and order someone to extend it upwards.  
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And put another bandage of linen thicker than the first bandage, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone, and extend the head so that you draw the corrupted flesh out from below, and uncover the flesh on the place where you see sinew, so that the sinew does not blanch the flesh.  
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And put a coal or a board under the bone to make the corrupted flesh rise up. 
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it is necessary to boil as much sinew as one can see and feel the corruption, and boil it again another time.  
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh. 
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then put a coal underneath, and then boil from one part to the other the corruption, and let the boiling be as long as the corruption is deep, as we have said.  
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then treat the corrupted joint, and the bone where it holds from the other side. 
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy than to treat both. 
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the wrist or ankle, it is a very serious matter, but nevertheless you must inquire into this ailment, how it reveals itself to you. 
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but make sure that the vein or nerve do not oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the instruments and saws for treating these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance, their thickness and thinness, their size and smallness, and their hardness. 
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason, it is necessary to have the appropriate instrument for each kind of work.  
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases. 
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	So prepare the instrument you need according to what is fitting. 
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder dislocates either from within or from without; 
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have medicine that will corrode it through the treatment of medicines, and it does not profit, then bind that limb up to the place where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes by this means death or malice, which is greater, from the lack of the limb; 
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and swells after the blackness, because the corrosion goes from limb to limb, and takes over the whole body; 
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hasten to cut it out, and if it is by the sting of some venomous creatures, such as a sea scorpion and an adder and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the vein, cauterize it, and do not give it any space to come as far as the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, cauterize it at the joint so that the corrosion does not come as far as the arm; 
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, cauterize it at the elbow; 
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the amount of its venom; 
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do the same thing when the corrosion comes to the foot: 
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, cauterize it after the other joint;  
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, cut off the whole foot; 
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, cut it at the knee joint;  
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; 
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And the way to cut or sew the limb is that you bind it above and below, and extend one minister the lower binding, and another minister the upper binding, and you sever the flesh between the two bindings at a span wide, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then cut or sew, and place on each side a linen cloth so that the sewing does not touch the healthy area, and causes the patient further injury and abscesses. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs while you are working, quickly cauterize the area or apply some restraining powders; 
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; 
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man in his left foot: 
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He had a blackness that looked like a burn, and this corruption first came in the back of his foot, until it spread throughout the whole foot; 
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corruption, he quickly covered the foot, and was healed; 
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And a long time afterwards the corruption returned to the back of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied things that drive it back after cleansing the body, and I could not stop the corruption; 
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of driving back the matter; 
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted that if I cut his hand, he would not die, because the strength of the man was weak; 
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; 
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I do not tell this except for the fact that one should do otherwise, if need be.  
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes in flesh, and remains so long that it makes a large gathering of pus; 
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and opens, and the pus flows out, and the wound remains empty, like some vessels; 
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is above it is also as delicate as fine linen cloths, and does not run down to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a sickness is called "healthy," and is not called "fistula"; 
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone completely, it is called a "fistula". 
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And the cook if it is such that you cut the whole skin around it, and likewise when it is thin, as a cloth. 
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And it does not spoil because of its putrefaction.  
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you believe that the skin will burn, and the putrefaction is not complete, and the skin is thick as leather, then cure it with an enema like this: 
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look if the breasts are large, and the belly that is in it has a foul smell, then give an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made like this: 
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take alum, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put them to cook in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;  
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take some according to your need, and make it with vinegar and honey, and apply it as a poultice on the breast, and draw out the purulence. 
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medicine in place for two hours, then remove it while squeezing.  
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times until the breast is softened and the pus is removed. 
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And sometimes apply a poultice of ash water when this medicine is not present, taking ashes from vine wood, pouring vinegar over them, then straining it and applying it as a poultice until you know the breast is well cleansed. 
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot bear the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then apply a poultice of vinegar and honey or one containing a bit of powdered litharge. 
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	Where you cleanse it with honey and mead wine, so that the honey has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine makes the healthy part air. 
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this, and you are certain that the breast is well purified, then cleanse it with something that produces flesh in it, and take a plaster that promotes healing, and make it with rose oil and wine. 
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	Or you cleanse it with certain medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken of the properties or treatise on ointments; 
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the opening of the breast is small, and the cannula of the enema cannot enter, then enlarge it a little with an iron instrument, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basil ointment, as long as it is enlarged. 
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too large, sew it up so that only the place where the enema can enter remains open; and if the opening that leads to the bowels is above, then make the cut lower than where it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the belly is in perfect condition, do not let flesh grow. 
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the breast below as you see it, arrange it in such a way that the belly runs to the lowest place where it is; for when the belly is perfect, do not let flesh grow and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see it, arrange it in this way. 
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	Let the belly run slightly downward, and do not let anything of the belly remain;  
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to draw out the health, and extend upon a linen sheet that covers all the health. 
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then cover as forcefully as possible the hole of the breast so that it is wider than the first, and extend ointment gently upon the other cloth according to the quantity of the hole, and place it upon the hole of the breast to align the belly, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once. 
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and he who is out the hole of the breast, often removes the bowels to know what runs from the bowels, whether it is venom or pus or enough, whether digested or undigested. 
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has extended in a certain way and you see the nature that leaps upon the hole of the breast, know that the breasts will soon heal, and health approaches. 
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, if you change another bandage, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast swells with undigested food after many days, know that the breast does not aerate.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons linger for a long time, do not despair of health, for healing approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose wounds heal slowly, and some who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if undigested bowels leap from the breast after many days, know that the breasts will not heal.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breasts are slow to heal and are extended, apply drying medicines in substance and dry in virtue, such as diachylon ointment, for there is a great part of vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine; 
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diachylon ointment, and make it with rose oil, and rosewater of old wine equal in substance; 
puis le confit et en use;	then cook it and use it;  
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same one made thicker when diachylon ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is off the fire; 
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then make it into a paste and spread it on the breast, and sometimes administer aristolochia longa, and roots of orchis mascula, which are also like flour of vetch and centaury; 
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in the use of simples or compounds: 
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	crush them, and make a powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and use it; 
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the sore is lengthened and is not cured by this remedy, then know that the corruption is thoroughly embedded, and makes an impression in the bone, or in hard limbs, or in ligaments; 
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the cure of fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A felon is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the hand or foot, or by chance arises in other places; 
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is envied, and no attention is paid to it, then it comes as a large abscess, running and dripping pus so much that it runs to the root of the nail, and by chance runs through all of it; 
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And corrosion comes to the bone, until there is a foul stench of pain, and the flesh around it becomes wide, and its color is dark. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the superfluity that remains from the ulcer, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauteries are very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; 
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses on the flesh and starts to grow, and the wound, then it is necessary that you put the point of a knife under the nail where it touches the flesh, and lift it up, and cut this flesh delicately and lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines on the remaining flesh to remove everything; 
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wounds until they are healed.  
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and treat it fiercely, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; 
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the flesh corrupting, cut it out in a manner as previously described, then treat it until it is healed; 
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and swollen, and he feels great pain, then you must first heal it. 
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the splint with a sharp knife across it, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the splint, for the patient would feel too much pain; 
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something on it that soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two growths that are born in the hands of some men are all fleshy, and sometimes there is bone where there is flesh, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of these are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in some of us of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those born in any part of the thigh do not move, and those born at the joint of the thigh may move; 
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of that which is fleshy is light, in a certain way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide splint. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those born at the root of the joint are difficult to heal:
si te tien dou coper.	you must hold it together.  
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one who is born or about to be born soon, it is fitting that you first shave the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for him, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Solderings which come together at the two ends come by birth, or by soldering of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you mend this suture so that it may repair according to its natural form. 
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or cloths softened in rose oil, so they do not stick together.  
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you can put between two thin slices of plum, as long as the wound is soldered, as it should be. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a soldering comes to any of his limbs with the palm, then cover that solder as it should be done.
des vils	of old
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large winding vessels full of melancholic superfluities which come from many parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.  
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purging with colocynth to him, and then apply balm of basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: 
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is where one cauterizes them and draws forth the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other method is that you bind the vein and draw out all the blood. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The length is according to this manner: 
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, raise the leg with hot water very strong, until the flesh becomes subtle, then strain the leg from the patient from above the thigh to the part below the knee; 
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, of a wide size, then loosen and draw forth the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the virtue of the patient can suffer; 
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then bind it, and command him to abstain from meats containing black bile; 
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin the evacuation and cleansing again when the veins are full, and it is of benefit to the patient.  
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The alleviations for this are according to this manner: 
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put him in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and swells the veins; 
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then apply the heated part to the vein near the head of the knee, or in the area below the ankle; 
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then apply the leather to the incision, and flay the vein from each side until it appears when touched; 
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters the leather it also appears white like a cord; 
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then push the vein down as far as it is raised from the leather, and then lift it lightly at the incision, then apply it to the other place above three times; 
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then flay the leather on top of the vein until it appears, then lift it with the vein as you did, and lift it at another incision, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then make another incision, or several if needed, then lift it and apply it to the calf of the foot, then pull and lift it up to the second incision; 
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract it piece by piece, until it is all out, then the cup. 
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot pull it out and lift it, then insert a needle at all its length doubled strong, tie it, and pull it, and insert it below the root, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out. 
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And be careful that it does not break off, for if it breaks off, one cannot pull it out or lift it, and harm comes to the patient. 
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have removed it all, put over the site of the wound wool softened in wine and rose oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and dress it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not break it. 
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts a vein, if it is curved and does not cut, let it cut the vein; 
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a large curve, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but let it be large as we have said, and this is the form: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is planted in legs, in warm parts where neither herbs nor trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; 
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the rot that comes under the skin, as it comes inside the body snakes and worms, plant between the skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very large inflammation comes in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude, just like a root of a plant.
