Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the shoulder opens, it is fitting that you wrap around a piece of linen from three and a half to two fingers, and tie it, and let the linen hang down on the leg, and every time it is damp with pus, wrap it around the linen, and tie it. 
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a portion and wrap the rest, and do not cut it at its root, until it is all out. 
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and rot or a wound, and evil sickness. 
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Because of this, it must be treated little by little until the end, and nothing should remain on the body. 
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And it sometimes happens that this vein when treated is ten palms long or even twenty, and a man once came to me to whom it was twenty palms long, and when you cut it, it will burst into one or more holes and pierce through to the bottom so that everything comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And let the matter inside be emptied, and apply to the area poultices that prevent putrefaction at any time, then treat it as you would an abscess. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never at this vein but two rain-drops, and likewise when it opens in the joint of the foot or leg and there comes a great deal of pus, and then it leaps rain. 
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure it then as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms which are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This illness is called in our land “ox disease,” because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well from limb to limb as long as it remains under the skin where it travels, and leaps hard; 
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it comes from putrefaction of certain humors, just as worms and snakes and lampreys and ascarides or roundworms come from the belly; 
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one fears its wickedness, because when it goes through the body and rises to the head, and comes to the eye, it may enter and destroy the eye; 
et ceu avient maintes fois.	And this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it heal and drain, you cannot force it except when it goes. 
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Therefore it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong tight bandage, then cut it above and drain it forcefully, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies. 
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm that it does is that it runs the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming or close to the eye, remove the eyebrow below it, then cut it above and drain it forcefully.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it is necessary to treat the patient with purifying medicines that dissolve harmful humors, and they should avoid meats that cause decay. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs, and then can move from limb to limb; 
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she revealed her arm to me, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; 
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and shortly after, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm to her shoulder, faster than anything, like living silver when it moves from one place to another; 
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that area and settled in her shoulder, and then shortly after ran throughout her body until it reached her other arm; 
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was turning again throughout her body, just as I saw.  
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I had seen many who claimed to move pain from place to place, but I had never seen it as clearly as I did in this woman; 
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought it was because the woman had a dry body and uncovered veins, and that is why this constrained wind appeared; 
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And it does not appear according to this reason in those who are fleshy and have moist bodies and filled veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this illness being healed, and the patient feels this pain as we have said, if it appears to you, immediately bandage it tightly above and below, then apply a poultice on top until this constrained wind leaves. 
et cauterize le leu;	And cauterize the place; 
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it at your own hands, then the cure of those who expel winds, such as foul-smelling pills and serpent pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of theirs is that there are some which have large points, and small ones, and bristling ones, and joined ones; 
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those which have two angles, and of those which have tongues, and of those where there are pieces; 
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And that which falls in no member falls according to two manners: 
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Where it falls in a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appear to you: 
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	It is fitting that you refrain from the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterward in several ways;  
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these evil signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not completely embedded, then treat it and care for the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the dura mater which is above the brain, is when there is dimming of sight and stupor and trembling and redness in it, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; 
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it is without strength from the nostrils, or ears; 
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps loses speech and voice; 
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there leaps from the wound white moisture resembling pus, and it also leaps like a burn from a chariot wheel;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, keep away from the treatment, and treat the arrow if it is not embedded. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of an arrow when it is lodged or stuck are that it is near the left breast, and also feels as if it were fixed in something hard, not empty; 
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow moves like a pulse, and dark blood flows from it, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: 
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Know then without doubt that death approaches.  
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that has not been removed is that without any discharge of pus it leaps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs deeply and desires cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow is lodged in the covering of the buttock, it is below the small ribs; 
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and gives great weariness and great pain and sighing; 
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and it moves all the members of the shoulders. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, by chance, some undigested meat may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow lodges in the belly or bowels, and no part of it sticks out through the intestines, there is no hope for a cure, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow lodges in the bladder, and the urine jumps and begins to flow, and the patient feels great pain: 
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the armpit and the spine of the back and the forearm and the thigh and the legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happens to a man that an arrow falls or pierces at the root of the nose:  
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and drew it out on the other side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any trouble. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I drew out an arrow for a man that had lodged in the fat of the eye below the eyelid, and the arrow was blunt, and one could only reach the point toward the fletching, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; 
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The player was healed, and no evil accident befell him. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I removed an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears:  
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the beard, and skillfully extracted it until I removed it, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I removed an arrow from a man, who had it stuck in his belly, and I thought he would die;  
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change at all; 
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow and pierced it, and removed it forcefully, and he did not suffer any ill effects. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw a man to whom an arrow had fallen in the back, and the wound was sealed over;  
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural state in any way, nor did it cause him harm in any of his natural functions. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sewn. 
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he remained thus without suffering great pain; 
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar cases. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And treat an arrow to a man of the princes, the king, which had fallen among his nose, and was sloping a bit toward the right side; 
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was all embedded. 
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat it after it had fallen three days. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I carefully tried to find it and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a throbbing and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I put on the place a poultice that was attractive and digestible so that the flesh would not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the arrowheads. 
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put on a plaster for several days and sewed up the wound thoroughly, and kept the patient for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead inside his flesh. 
et il le me dist.	And he told me so. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put a caustic medicine on the wound for several days until it was open and I tried it and felt the head of the arrow stirring in its place.  
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I widened the opening of the wound with that caustic medicine until the head of the arrow became visible to me. 
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and carefully worked the edges for four months, and then enlarged the wound so that I could put in the forceps and pull it from one side and the other, but it would not come out. 
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then I did not cease to refine and devise ways of instruments until I made them one day with well-made forceps, according to their shape which will come at the end of this chapter, so that I could pull it out and restore the wound.  
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the master judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored. 
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your treatment on those which I do not say, for books cannot contain everything. 
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But wise masters compare on very few things, and on those which are present and lacking, they find nine works and nine instruments for the removal of foreign things that happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not leave the limbs where they are lodged except according to two manners: 
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	Either by the place where they enter, or by another part;  
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which leaves further by the place where it enters is an arrow entering their flesh, and it leaves hardly ever now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, leave it until the flesh around it is rotten, and the exit is clear. 
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it each day. 
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Then it will jump out, and if it does not, pierce around it with a very fine tool until the flesh around it is enlarged, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: 
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not treat it, but leave it until it is equal after several days, for if the arrow reaches as far as the brain, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed further than in the bone alone, and does not reach as far as the synovial cavity, and the patient remains for some days without any ill accident, then you may draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very stuck like this and cannot come out by force, then administer poultices around it, as I have told you. 
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place until it is healthy.  
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in a place in the body so that it cannot be seen, then one must seek it entirely. 
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, remove it with any suitable instrument; 
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot, because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then widen it until the wound is large; 
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and remove the arrow if you can, and if there are ears on it by which it is held, then cut away the flesh that is stuck to it in two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can pull it out. 
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and subtly, even though you do not break the arrow, draw it out more easily. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it be until the sinews around it are ripe, then treat it, for extraction will bring relief.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then apply what we have said about wound treatment in its chapter.  
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting a nerve or vein, and place something as you can move to draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; 
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow fell upon them, for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place them according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	An arrow that has come from another direction, or where it appears there is something of it, or the skin is swollen in a place where one can see or feel it apparently: 
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut on top, so that the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	if a leap is possible now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then begin the extraction again until it comes out.  
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if there is an arrow shaft in it, push it through the whole shaft 
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	And if it is bone, and you see that the pushing will be difficult, then use an instrument with a point, so that the tip of the arrow enters into the point of the instrument. 
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	Then push it in, and if the arrow is pointed, push the instrument with its point entering inside to make the extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is fitting that you cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as is appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is bone or lead or in the belly or bladder or the side, and it is close, and you can cover over it, then cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And be careful not to cover a vein or nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the healing as long as it is healthy. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs with which one treats arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways: 
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the end of the arrowhead is like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrow, as this is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the forceps for pushing and for knowing if it is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are XXXI veins from which one heals, of which there are XVI chiefs, namely: 
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two beaters that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; 
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in two apparent temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two tears of the two eyes, which are called "aspirers"; 
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is on the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the head of the nose; 
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two gullets that are at the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the mouth on the lips, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; 
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And you see those veins that are under the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly draws blood are five in each arm: 
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and common people call it "the vein of the head"; 
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "fascia," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and common people call it "the vein of the heart"; 
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and common people call it "the vein of the belly," and it is above the ulna bone, and it is the one from which we draw blood, which appears clearly above the hollow. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvation is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins: 
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the curve of the pouch on the left side, and the second is at the ankle on the right side; 
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; 
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein that is behind the ears helps with old catarrhs, and migraines; 
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of bloodletting, as I have told you, are that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; 
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tighten the patient's neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places hanging from the head; 
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Place your hands on your side, and where you feel the pulse below your side, that is a sign of incision. 
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet and insert it below the vein to the bone. Then lift your hand along the whole vein upwards, cutting both the skin and the vein well - it must go through twice - and make the blood flow until you see it. 
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then bind and bandage it tightly until it is healed. 
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And as I have already said in the first book, incision and cautery.  
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The cutting of the two arteries located in the temples is good for old migraines, headaches, and habitual ophthalmia, and for a flow of hot tears. 
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of bloodletting are as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And this is so that the patient tightens his neck until the two veins appear openly. 
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and they feel the pulse beneath your thumb, and then sign to hold. 
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then lift the heart onto the vein at the top with your index finger and insert the lancet beneath it, lift the vein upward, and cut it, just as you did for the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need. 
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then untie the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.  
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And then bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed. 
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction, which is the beginning of this book.  
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic for ancient diseases of the face, and migraine, and redness.  
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is such that the patient twists their neck until the vein appears; 
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur," of which this is the form: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let blood flow out according to the quantity you see; 
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is dry, never leaving the ligature for a long time with a wide flame.  
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, the flame should not be too strong; 
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the ligature must not be twisted sideways, because the bone is nearby and it might break if the flame is too thin.  
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	Ligating the two veins that are in the temples helps with the eyes, and with tingling, redness, and pain in the face; 
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is such that the patient tightens his neck by twisting with some cord, as before; 
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the cautery, and whether the cautery is through or long, a peck long and a peck wide, because there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is subtle, it may break; 
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then let blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind on cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The cautery of the vein in the nose is good for fever and for strong headache, and for facial ailments such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, even when it is old. 
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the cautery is such that the patient tightens his neck, then he pulls his nose to your left hand, and take a long subtle flame, and put it between the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow. 
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too far with force, and let it run blood according to your need, then bind it for a night, for it is very quickly restored. 
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the form of the flame:  
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The sinew of two guindeges helps in the constriction of the urethra, and at the beginning of menstruation, and for many diseases, and for itching, and for corrosion, and for herpes, and for estiomenes; 
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the sinew is such that the patient tightens their neck under one and the other, as we have said.  
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And let the masters be standing upon the head of the patient, and the patient sit upon a seat, then sinew the vein along a good distance widely, then draw out blood moderately, or as much as is needed. 
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then redo it on the other vein, then untie the ligature, and remove all the veins moderately, so that the patient doesn't strangle. 
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	And leave him until morning, so that the wound may heal. 
de la sainie des leivres	From the sanctity of books
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The vein of the lips above helps with coal in the mouth and corruption of gums and fissures of the lips and pain and swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the healing is to make the patient sit in front of you, and remove their collar as I have said; 
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn back the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them are small black veins: 
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	therefore cut one and the other, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, then cut the largest of each side, and also do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the vein below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The vein under the tongue helps after the head vein is bled, and it is for the constriction of the throat and diseases of the eye and mouth. 
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the bleeder is such that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a black vein.  
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Bleed one and then the other, and do not go too deep because underneath are the arteries.  
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the arms which we commonly bleed are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	Either by striking with a sharp instrument like a lancet or a thin olive-wood tool as sharp as a knife, and it is called an "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins filled with thick blood which appears, and that contain thick and troubled blood. 
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And this is the form of the olive flame: 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more delicately pointed, and it is for cauterizing delicate veins, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses that are below the throat, and at the neck, and at the chest, and at the belly. 
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is fitting for the healer that he bleeds it well, and that he guards against the artery which is below.  
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it is fitting to staunch it, as I have said; 
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame must not be pointed but cutting like a knife.  
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then it is fitting that you extract it and change another; 
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	Where you want any vein of it, or you make a vein in place of it on the arm: 
elle apert manifestement;	It opens manifestly; 
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the cautery is applied to the flame, as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the vein, it is fitting then that you take hold of the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse; 
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with a cut, and then bind the arm, and cauterize the vein with the flame; 
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful that you do not strike the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is of the artery: 
eschui la donques.	Avoid it then. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protrude upwards as the urine of a child, and its blood is red and thin, know that it is the sinew of an artery:  
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and place your hand on its length, then remove your hand if it does not stick, which often happens. 
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Bind the arm, and leave it thus, and let the patient not move it. 
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.  
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood is not clotted and it flows, and no medicine is present for you, then bind the artery when it appears, because it is the head of the removal. 
et estainche li sans.	And clot the blood. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a bark of fig, and split it, and take one of the halves and bind it well until the next day. 
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the blood clots, that is good.  
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If not, if the wound cures, as we have said, use powders which clot blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the bandages are not tied too tightly in several ways because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's binding. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein in the middle of the arm helps it draw blood from above the head and below the body because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said. 
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it is necessary for the phlebotomist to be careful of the nerve that is below and if he pricks too deeply and finds the nerve it will swell and the bloodletting will be tightened and perhaps it cannot heal. 
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve appears many times and if it does not appear in some men because of its subtlety, then you must draw blood from the instrument numb. 
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid the nerve as best you can. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make the incision long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The sinew of the cephalic vein helps so much that it draws blood from the head and helps them. 
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is fitting to bleed by pricking with olive oil flame or myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all the veins, for it has neither nerve nor artery beneath. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one must seek out the lightest place, and do not grieve if one misses the first time, and one begins again. 
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance some men's veins swell when pricked for the first time but it does not matter.  
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing that you must know about bleeding is that it is not administered except to preserve health and to avoid illnesses to come.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	And let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins which are these.  
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	That is to say, cephalic, basilic, and median cubital. 
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must bleed at the beginning of spring in young people, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; 
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	And one must bleed on the first day or the third, after two hours or three on the day. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding which is administered for illnesses has no set time, but only when need be, by day or by night, in all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not fitting to bleed children until 14 years old, nor women carrying a child except from the fourth month until the seventh.  
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Those who have passed sixty years should not bleed themselves.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wants to be bled, in whatever way it may be, it is fitting that they cleanse their bowels with a light enema, if they have much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines harmful superfluities damaging the principal limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor does he who is too full of meat heal, nor he who is drunk, as long as it lasts, nor those with dropsy. 
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And it worsens one who is treated after colic, fever, discharge from the belly, and frequent intercourse for a woman, and labor, staying awake and fasting, and those who lose their strength, or by something of the weapon or body. 
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtle the humors, if it is thick, by meats and drinks and by medicines, if you have the power. 
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter a bath, if nothing forbids it, to make the blood thinner, and let it bleed from the vein of the left arm near the third rib, as we have said.  
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard yourself that day from work, and straining, and lust, and similar things; 
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be bound and joined, and let the bandages be higher than those on which one is bandaged, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the bandage moderately, for when it is too tight or too loose, it cannot correct the sinew. 
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	Then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and are felt.  
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the bandages with a drop of old oil, then put your index finger of your left hand on that vein below the place where he wants to bandage it, so that the vein does not go and fail when cutting.  
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee as ropes in a bandage, and if there are such ones that are full of windiness, so that when you put on the flame, it withdraws from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus one is among them. 
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, if the wound is too narrow, therefore it is fitting that the barbers be informed in these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; 
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, begin again a little lower than that place or higher quickly, if the veins are not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the veins are swollen and the patient is afraid, let it rest for a day or two, and do not bind the arm: 
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps some abscesses will come; 
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter a bath, then begin the bleeding again if it pleases him; 
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the puncture is small, or the blood runs subtly and you doubt that it will not issue as much blood as you see, stick into that puncture itself with all your might. 
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work quickly so that the veins are swollen; 
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the lancing again, and put a poultice of oil on it, for it draws the body's blood, and oil is gentler in this place than lye. 
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the oil poultice to each vein you lance, to staunch the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same thing makes a triangle and bowl of it, when it is placed on the spot. 
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if the blood is too thin it separates when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, even when it has not been lanced before except at this time when the opening of the vein is small, hurry and put a sponge soaked in hot water and salt on the spot for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has been released from the vein, and if it remains in place after several days without any blackness or greenness, then do not harm it. 
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see it, put some aloe or myrrh mixed in calamint juice, mustard, or something similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there are abscesses and swelling at the incision of the basilica: 
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Then put your hand on it, and if you find the area soft when pressing with your hand, then that swelling is bad. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore, be careful not to put anything of what we have said on it, for you might cut into an artery by accident. 
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But apply a dry plaster to harden the area, and then treat it with another dressing until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red; 
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see it thick, let it flow until it is thin; 
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, let it cool down. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is fitting for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, that a larger wound be made, and the incisions be wide; 
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for one who is weak, do the opposite, and they should be bled a little and often, and one should bleed them by cutting across, not by pricking. 
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bleeding is safe from running of blood and cutting of nerves, and is worth more than bleeding that is long or wide. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for one whose body is lacking in bloodletting, it is fitting to give soft bread with pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is hot, draw blood three or four times. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after the outflow of much blood, it is fitting that he inhales broth of flesh and fragrant subtle syrup and uses other things as we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to heal his arm and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds a little at a time, according to the quantity of his continuing strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bandage their arm after the first bleeding, and they have strong flesh, then they should bandage seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal from another injury, it must heal on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For it has much blood within the body which is already heated, and brings fever; 
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the opening so that it discharges in streams; 
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	after you have observed all the conditions of health, and place your hand on his pulse when he is well, so that death does not come in place of streams, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; 
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not fitting when you see the arm loosen, and make the blood come out the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	and if it is crooked, let him extend his arm quickly, for this would be bad; 
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but leave it until it heals the second time;  
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you put the tip of the flame there, until the blood which is frozen at the opening of the vein comes out strong, and place on it a bit of salt recently made into lye, and press lightly on it. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then do so in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein at the elbow is cut instead of the vein at the temple because it is thicker.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the healing is such that the patient plunges their hand into hot water, until the pulse is red. 
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it is bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then the healing is maintained crosswise, not wide nor long. 
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And the opening should be wide, and it should be healed very close to the joint of the hand, and if none can come out, put the hand back into hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough. 
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is summer, do not put the hand back into hot water at all, for one puts it more in winter than in summer. 
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And this vein's healing is safer than all other veins, because there is neither artery nor nerve.  
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the salvation vein of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: 
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and plunge it into hot water, until the vein is swollen if you see it. 
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if it deviates sideways, and if you cut it all the way through, it will not matter.  
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath all naked of flesh, and then put the hand back into hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.  
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, put oil and wax on the vein to heal quickly, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sinew of the left hand is worth against the disease of the mouse, and do all as I have told you to the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The vein of the saphenous is worth more than all the diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of phlegm, and disease of the kidneys, and thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its bleeding is such that the patient plunges his foot into hot water and rubs on the vein until it bursts, and binds above the joint of the foot.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And the vein is at the ankle, and there are many veins that run up above the foot. 
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	So bleed from the largest vein, or at the ankle, which is worth more.  
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it on the foot, beware of the nerves underneath, and heal it through as in cutting. 
et soit li flaimes anesil.	Let the flame be extinguished. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the cautery fails the first time, begin the second a little higher up, for the flesh is salty. 
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about nerves as we have said, and so do the same to the saphenous vein of the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle bone, and its pain is worth the pain of the hip when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of its cautery is that the patient enters a bath and squeezes above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open. 
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, cauterize it in all ways that you can and crosswise.  
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is worth more for you to cut it, for the flesh is dry and it is much replenished by most men. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, look for no vein that appears or back of the foot, and toward the little toe, and beware of the nerves; 
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And draw as much blood as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put cotton on it and remove it; 
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	from cupping glasses
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cups are made of horn, or of ivy, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And cupping is done in two ways: 
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting. 
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping which is done without cutting is according to two methods:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Either it is with all fire, or without fire; 
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And cupping which is done by cutting and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is all over the head; 
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are hammered onto the neck; 
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the others on both sides of the neck; 
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping glass below the chin;  
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cupping glass on both shoulders; 
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glass on the loins; 
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cupping glasses hammered onto both arms;  
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cupping glasses on both legs; 
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping glasses on both ankles; 
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cupping does not draw blood, except for a few small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this it does not weaken anyone, as one does when bleeding from a vein; 
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither with much heat nor little heat, in any illness that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it is necessary due to illness to apply cupping, or for custom, then we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and every time. 
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; 
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness as well; 
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood; 
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And there are some who faint, and see by night blood and sorrow and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is less than a month old, we order him to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The juice of the mulberry helps with the heaviness of the head ... that comes from it, and it is not right for this to be after the evacuation of all the body; 
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this cupping is done in place of the bleeding from the head veins, and it is not suitable for those of cold complexion to use, or who have diarrhea, for it does them great harm. 
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore it is not suitable for the elderly to use it, nor those who have or primarily cold diseases.  
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover often become stiff, and therefore it is necessary to put the cupping glass a little lower because of the risk of stiffness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Cupping on the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the basilica vein, and therefore it is good for the constriction of the breast, and for the rupture of the anal canal, and for all coughs, and for repletion. 
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is not good to leave it on too long, for if it holds too tightly it can cause prolapse or obstruction of the stomach and the heart.  
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Cupping on the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of bleeding from the basilica vein.  
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is necessary that you order the patient to press his hand at its placement so that he does not strike the artery and blood does not flow. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	Cupping below the chin is good for diseases of the mouth, and decay of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; 
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is placed on the two lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping of the shoulders is good for illnesses that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	Cupping on the thighs is as good as three veins in the arms, for it draws blood from these large veins; 
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and order the patient not to make too much effort, for the flesh is thin and under it are nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cup placed on the rump is good for hemorrhoids in the buttocks and illnesses below, and it is necessary that the cup be large, and be made of horn, so that it draws well; 
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it were delicate, it would break 
et i fai grans plaies.	and it would make large wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The cupping glasses on the legs bleed freely because they draw blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains of the loins, and of the bladder, and soften inflammations.  
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are placed on the two thighs and the two ankles; moreover, they weaken the body after a long time, and cause emaciation in several conditions.  
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply a cupping glass is that you first put it empty and suck gently, then place it quickly and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and see the redness of the blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then let it rest and put the cupping glasses back on, and take care in the disposition of bodies, because there are some who have thick flesh and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a deep puncture; 
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: 
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to make subtle the way of thick blood.  
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; 
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw blood drop by drop, we only make one incision.
