Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, we often restart; 
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, we strike deep, and the end is that the heart be pierced only slightly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have few pores, that you moisten the rims of the cups with oil that is stimulating and dissolving: 
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is so, with oil of violets, or with oil of sweet almonds, or with oil of pumpkin seed; 
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in winter, with oil of watercress, or lily, or chamomile, or another similar one. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or balm, or oil of anise, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person whom one heals has tender flesh and large pores, it is not fitting to put any oil on them, but they should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or water of blackthorn, or water of pumpkin, or water of porcelain, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, should rise with rosemary, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities may rise with old wine, or vinegar water, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar ones; 
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it is not suitable to apply a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; 
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he washes himself when he is about to be cupped and when he has been cupped. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are being treated if they are choleric, and if the skin is too raw and inflamed;  
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is fitting that he takes cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in the summer, and similar things 
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat little, and meat from a young animal, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, should take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine midway between old and new, and eat little, and eat little and small birds and pigeons; 
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he will bleed, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is fitting to give some men at times three-spice or nutmeg before the bleeding, or after, to strengthen the main limbs; 
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the wine be subtle, but it does not suit those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cupping glasses that are put without cutting are those that are put on the liver, and on the thigh, and gout, and on the belly and the buttocks and the loins and the hip, for these members do not suffer to be cut on them, and we only do it for attracting blood from one member to another, just as we put them on the breasts when a newborn bleeds; 
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put cupping glasses on the belly and on the shoulder to reduce the limb; 
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an inflammation or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the inflammation, or dislodges the stone from its place. 
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And it does so when you put it on the liver and on the thigh when there is retained windiness, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to only suck. 
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of hot water, as in illnesses of the pleura, and in such a way one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or hot water in which herbs suitable for this have been cooked. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two widths and a half palm of length, and has at the cost side around the middle a small hole, as for putting in a needle, and is made of horn, smooth beforehand so that it does not hurt the patient when placing it on the limb; 
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and have a rod of wood or iron in the middle, to put a candle holder on it, and they are big and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them 
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cupping glasses for children are different than those for the old, and for the thin than for the fat.  
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus put this cupping glass upon the limb: 
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the candle holder of wax or linen, and put it through the cupping glass through the rod which is in the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient; 
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it upon the limb, and your two hands must be upon the part that we have said, so that when you want to remove it, if the steam goes out, one takes off the cupping glass
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the linen as before and start again often, if you need to. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	For the cupping glass which is administered in the illness of pleurisy, for all acute conditions, it has neither a stem nor a perforation, and is only applied when full of water, and is placed upon the limb only. 
et c’est li forme:	And this is its form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Cupping glasses are only applied to limbs where one cannot apply cupping glasses due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places. 
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in those places devoid of flesh, such as the bone or nails, and other similar ones. 
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the quality of the cupping glass is such that when you find cupping glasses which are in a sweet and clear liquid without any impurity, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And place them for one night in a sweet liquid, so that they become familiar and have nothing inside their bellies. 
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then let it be bled by vein and cupping glass, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on bandages. 
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full and begin to shrink, if it is a place where one can put a cupping glass, then put it on, for this is worth much afterward. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place gently, and then sharply, very well, and then splint it. 
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the bandages become too tight after the body swells under them, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put it on top until the bandages are loosened. 
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are many bandages, put powdered vitriol or alum, and similar things on top until they loosen. 
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you can place half a handful of peeled beans on the spot and leave them until they burn there, this will stop it now. 
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other herbs. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the herbs do not want to be taken, rub the place with fresh blood, or stick a needle in it until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will burn; 
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are falling off, powder a piece of aloe and salt crushed up, or ashes, then they will fall off now. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, young son, that the crazy things I write in this chapter, you will never see them in any of the old books, nor read about them in letters; 
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is strange in our land, because I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I don't know anything else except by the knowledge of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated them with science, and through experimentation, and through the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are needed, as I have done in these two previous chapters. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is fitting then that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of speech and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and stays upon virtue, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is fitting that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, unless something prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age;  
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the time is very bad, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and avoid cold foods, that is to say cold stews, and broth of birds and goats, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess, or spreading of matter in the limb; 
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to his first government which he had used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is fitting that one nourish the patient with foods that promote fattening, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in broth, rice, and peas, and veal feet, and cow's udder, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at half breaking it can return to its place more quickly than a fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot be well set or rejoined according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor can those which are too tender, such as the bones of small children; 
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but have no care, set upon the broken bone large splints which bind and join the limb together, until it is strengthened as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not stop his work, and for this, it is necessary to nourish him with large meats as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to splintering, and others to sharpening, just as the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every manner, let him have his engine and his own instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the bone is broken because the limb is twisted, and appears clearly by itself, and makes a sound when pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is neither crookedness nor sound at the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture. 
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But there may well be crookedness, or a crack, or a small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not fitting that you move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come hereafter, and then now subtly extract it.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture which goes in a direction, and are the two parts separated, it is necessary now to put them back together equally, just as boils heal. 
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if a boil comes hot, let it be left alone for a day, until the boil is calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it equal to the pus that you can lightly and gently draw out, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restorations of those where there are pieces.  
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then remove it, as is appropriate afterward. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into two pieces, whether it is an arm or leg, or at the hand, if it is a small limb, or two tendons, or one tendon and at the hand; 
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural shape so that when the broken parts of the limb are freed, you will reset all additions in their places as much as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient. 
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and properly adjust the two ends of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right:  
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if it is set well, do not force it too much, nor press as those who cause boils, heat and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have often seen. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is set properly, warn the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and be sure that the limb is so secure that he does not feel any pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, except perhaps a little, it is necessary to put him in a position where he feels no pain. 
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And be careful that he is placed straight so that crookedness does not occur when it is being restored. 
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in size, shape, and severity.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar ones: 
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: 
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and strong bandage, because wide bandages embrace the whole large limb and restrain it equally on all sides so that there is no indentation. 
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie on top light strips of linen, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a bit on all the bandage, then go above the break and tighten it less so that the break is then moved away a little from the break. 
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament bit by bit, until you grasp a large portion of the healthy area, then take hold of the other ligament and turn it back around over the broken area 
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the break, and extract it moderately, neither too strongly nor too gently, as we have said in the first place above; 
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the ligaments strips of linen or cloths, as long as they are all equal, then bind everything above with bandages, and then apply your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something soothing and hot on it to remove the swelling, and leave it like that for several days; 
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then remove your splints, and they should be half the width of a walking stick, or made of wood from which shingles are made, or palm ribs, and they should be according to this shape: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is fitting that the star that one puts on the fracture be a bit larger and wider than the others 
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and it should also be as long as is fitting for the limb, whether small or large; 
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then remove it from the stars as you did in the first hour, then tie a thread over it neatly, as was done in the first hour on the fracture; 
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is bound, the less pain there will be; 
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is fitting that the thread be of medium thickness, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;  
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their ligatures with twisted linen cord, it is a great error, for the ligature cannot be even if it is too fine, and it is not fitting that there be less than two fingerbreadths of space between each star. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore from the heads of the bones after tightening them in their joints, put under them cloths of flax, or wool scraps, so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the heart is broken, I will say its cure hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to set all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not fitting to put strong splints on before 5 or 7 days, or more according to your judgment of the hot abscess which appears; 
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And see here this manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: 
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And it is that you take flour which clings to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and make this mixture neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, for this is the common way to make a plaster for restoring fractures in many positions, as well for women as for young children, for it is not too harsh nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way to make a plaster for restoring fractures and dislocations and twists: 
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take 3 drachms of frankincense, myrrh, and asafoetida, and gum arabic and mastic, each 10 drachms.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Myrrh and aloes, each five drachms. 
alechil VIIII З.;	Alkanet, nine drachms. 
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And make them into powder, and mix them with the white of an egg;  
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the man's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and is worth much to many men.  
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another kind of plaster that is good for sprains: 
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mugwort and betony, each ten drachms.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Myrrh and aloes, each nine drachms. 
acaice VI З.;	Agrimony six drachms.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Boiled Armenian bole ten drachms, and grind well, and cook with vinegar or the white of an egg, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another kind of plaster for joints and bones separated from their places, to ease pain arising, and they use this plaster on the bone and break. 
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new linen cloth, and moisten it with oil and boiled oil, and place it on the area. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for calming a hot abscess, and properly removes pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to make a plaster that restores broken bones: 
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and common poppy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture and to soften the remnant of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take marshmallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, of each one part; 
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind it, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or plain water, and use it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another kind of plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take marshmallow root, flax seed, betony, melilot, and tansy, and violet flowers and chamomile flowers, of all one part; 
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind it, and steep with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb for restoration except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that one must put on the broken limb, to restore things dry a hot poultice, such as myrrh and aloe and frankincense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way of plaster which is good for injury and pain: 
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and horsehair cut off, or bird feathers, and visnaga, and grind them equally, and make a plaster and bind it. 
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then unbind it a little while after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that the bone has moved from its place;  
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not, do not unbind it for several days. 
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, or lack of rest or swelling, then hurry and unbind it, and remove the plaster now; 
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take light linen cloth, and a damp sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift the place, until the itching stops, and the pain is calmed;  
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen on top, soaked in water or rose oil, and tie it over a bandage, until you are sure of a warm abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and rest the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the subtle binding, and apply a bit of plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before. 
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and subtly until it is healed.  
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess grows and reddens and has pain and swelling is gone entirely, and you need plaster and bandage, if it starts again as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing comes to the limb from what we have said, do not unbind it for more than three days or four or five or seven. 
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And never leave it for twenty days, according to what you see, until the fracture heals and approaches the adjustment of the flesh. 
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Then restrain more than before, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before. 
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see the place drying up more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come.  
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Therefore apply a hot compress, every time you unbind it, and this be every third day, and loosen the bandage a bit. 
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this work therefore cut the bindings on the limb, and quickly amend what the foolish mirror does, that twists the limb back again.  
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is evil, and if the work is dangerous, I see no other thing than to let it be and do it straight. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of fractures, and diverse figures, and the causes are destined.  
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures that are made from the percussion of a sword, and the neck breaks all the bone up to the sinew that is beneath the bone, as a hatchet or club does.  
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And because of this, this manner of fracture is called “hatchet blow." 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the sword strikes the bone above without piercing, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And the wound from these two fractures is large or small.  
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or a crack, or chips of stone, or a chair on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture penetrating close to the membrane which is under the bone, or on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if a wound that is rejoined to the bone as fine as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary"; 
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone or by falling, or by a similar thing, and it causes the piece of bone to go down, and the edges are shaved like the way blacksmiths shave when they sharpen on anvils; 
si entre li piere dedens.	if the stone enters inside.  
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have soft bones, such as children's skulls; 
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are separated like tiles. 
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I will speak about them in their place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by traction on them, and inquiry with probes, and by the corrupted flesh which is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The likeness of hair is known by this, that when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs strongly upon it, if the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, pay attention to the patient's conditions, and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, spasms, pallor, fever with chills, and the eyes coming out and reddening, and other similar things in various states, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeless situation, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the nettle rash first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the time that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone is corrupted, and accidents come as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the fractured part thus: 
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you take the head of the sick person nearby and uncover above the bone in all the ways that you can and above the figure of the wound more often than you can and if discharge of blood comes to uncovering the bone or abscess forms, then help him with what is necessary and it is that you fill the place with cloths softened in rose oil; 
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the abscess forms are appeased and be sure of discharge of blood; 
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two manners of work: 
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one manner is if you cut a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is if you have a number of diverse incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and are of hard iron.  
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And work lightly so that you do not bruise the head. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce it around, so that you administer cuts with chisels, but make sure they do not pierce beyond the bone of the tester, and it must have a margin or circle on top so that the point does not pass beyond the bone. 
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	And you must have several of them so that each one comes into its place according to the type of bone, so that you have chisels for all types. 
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three kinds of chisels: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place the chisel on the bone and turn it back and forth until you know the bone is pierced. 
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put the chisel in another place a little after and do the same all around, then cut with chisels the space of bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand or to any of the instruments that you have such as tongs, pincers; 
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and guard that you do not touch the brain or the spinal cord. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is fitting that you restore the instrument which has remained from the bone to all the other instruments resembling an incisor, but it must be more slender and more subtle than the other incisor.  
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if there remains nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, then gently remove them with instruments. 
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other manner of working is that which Galien mentions, which is safer;  
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he praises it very highly, and that is his word. 
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a portion of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lentiform incision tool, which has this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, but divide the part into two sides so that the cutting is towards the bone.  
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike lightly with a small mallet on top so that you gently tap the bone all around and be careful of the cloth underneath. 
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is near the bone, strike lightly, for one can strike the bone well without harm and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the cloth, and the bone is cut only on top, and there are small pieces, then you must grind behind that roughness, and remove the scales with a subtle razor which you must have in various quantities, so as to administer the most suitable one in each place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you shave before with great razors, and afterwards with more subtle ones, and do not cease to do this until it is good.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other delicate cuttings and breaks, it is fitting that you administer aid according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that cannot be answered by one who has not put their study into this art. 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the break is exposed, it is fitting that you take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it upon the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it upon the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as lightly as you can so that you do not strain the suture then apply another bandage over it and do not bind it too tightly just enough to hold the wound; 
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess has subsided then untie it and apply medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, frankincense powder, birthwort, and similar things 
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make a powder from these things and put it on the wound and then apply cleansing medicines without biting. 
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and make sure the wound is always clean and do not leave any ointment on it nor allow pus to gather because when pus collects on the bandage covering the brain it will run and harden and cause the patient great harm;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when you put something biting on the suture it irritates it above.  
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come except for the medicine that has been put on it, so that its virtue may have effect, then you must take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and in this glue one cloth and lay it upon the surface. 
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it in ways that are fitting until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, for these are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is forced to bend or twist, and then it heals. 
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is fitting that you bind your little finger or thumb to the nose and put the broken part equally inside your index finger, and in the pouch by force, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and make sure the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and the bone cannot come back into place, then you must put it equal to the head of a nail, a large prick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, redo it in the same way, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; 
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess that has formed is calmed, then bind at the head of the two ends with linen cloths, if the break is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you bind the other side, if the break is there; 
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the openings of the bone.  
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some healers say that one must soften the bandages with butter and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem right to me, but it is necessary that they are softened in a mixture of egg yolk and mill dust;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the bandage on until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And at no time should one put goose feathers in place of tents, and if a cloth bandage is wrapped around it, hold the fracture, and let the patient breathe. 
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or do what you see fit. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come up while you are working on them, put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a drop of diammonium.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not come to a head, apply a plaster made from chickpea flour and frankincense powder, mixed with egg white, then place it on light cloths, and do not bind it tightly. 
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments for this purpose, then stitch the wound and treat it with things that promote healing flesh and bones, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this. 
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the bone, treat it with tents and apply splints of wood until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only superficial, and not broken in two, but pushed inward, so a connoisseur can slightly recognize it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; 
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left jawbone, then put your right index finger and gently push the fracture inward, and hold it with the other hand by pressing, and set it equal. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts, so that it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or breakage, then bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place cerate on the broken jawbone, and place a double cloth on top; 
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place on top of the cloth a large well-made splint, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it up at the points that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.  
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, then untie it on the third day, and then reset what has changed; 
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put plaster on top, made from flour from the mill with plenty of egg or sesame flour after you have removed the cerumen. 
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put light wool on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed; 
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	It is often healed in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, do as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see that no part of the bone is removed;  
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if you are removing it subtly, use suitable instruments for this. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, if the wound is wide, and put on it bandages suitable for that, to promote flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	Of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The clavicle breaks several times in front of the shoulder and the fracture can be in three ways: 
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	either it is broken and detached into two, with fragments, and this is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a fracture with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is this when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the broken bone is. 
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the side. 
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then set the fracture to your liking, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor protrusion. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and make it large according to your need. 
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And extend and lift the broken bone, and remove the sphere with your hand, so that you set the fracture as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder back out because it has come in perfectly, then it is fitting that the patient lies often on his backside, and puts under the shoulder a medium pillow, and have the assistants push the shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then straighten the fracture to your liking, and if you find it broken apart, it is necessary that you cleave open. 
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and treat the parts lightly, and if the bone cannot join for any pressure, then use the blade of one of your incisors. 
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but put under it this instrument, to hold the joint:  
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not sharp, and should be as wide as the bone requires, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work;  
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two jaws, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, as is the break in the wound that you made when treating the bones.  
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of the hot abscess, if the wound is large and the break is small or if you doubt the hot abscess, then cover the wound with bandages and splints, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, soak a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and without fractures, is that you put on the bone a plaster of flour from the mill and egg yolk, and put light cloths on top, and put a splint below the armpit if you need it. 
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large bandage a palm wide, then put two layers of linen on the cloths and plaster; 
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a slender splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down;  
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the splint on the fracture, and wind the bandage up the neck, and below the healthy armpit, and below the injured armpit; 
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And bind each part well, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the splint does not move on the broken bone, then leave it alone for a day, and when the bandages loosen, retighten them; 
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps put a small bolster under the armpit to raise the shoulder. 
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if it lightens the fracture of the collarbone by lifting the shoulder, then you bind his arm to his neck and do not untie it until 20 days have passed so that no evil accident occurs.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then you begin the plaster again, if you see he needs it, and take it off and leave it like that until he is restored. 
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it is restored at most in 28 days, and less for some men.  
de la brisure de l’espaule	From the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Sometimes the shoulder breaks or dislocates so badly that it cannot be set straight except by touch. 
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If you set the limb according to the shape of the fracture and reset it according to its natural form in all ways that you can. 
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put on the place powder from the mill with plenty of egg white, and light bandages, and put a double cloth on top. 
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put on a wide and fine splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if below the splint there is hair in any place of the shoulder, use that hair as a bandage of linen, so that the splint sits evenly. 
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then bind it all tightly with a large bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and examine the binding each day.  
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it loosens, bind it again and set the splint equally if it has moved from its place, and have the patient lie on their side. 
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder will be restored in 20 days or 25. 
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is fulfilled, untie it and be sure, for it is not bone that moves lightly. 
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out before, and not below the heart, then lift it up, and bind it with splints, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to soothe a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is sometimes broken in two, but this rarely happens. 
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	But it often breaks at the ends. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken below, it declines downward, and the patient feels great pain, and shortness of breath, and everything else, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the hair in the broken bones, and they see it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and he puts a cushion between his shoulders, then presses on the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides with his hands, and subtly tries to make them equal in all ways as much as he can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; 
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then he puts on plasters and bandages above the bone with a fine powder of salt or some other light substance, and wraps it in a cloth and ties it over the broken bone so that it does not move. 
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And he turns the bandage around the back and removes it carefully, and examines the bandage every hour and if it is loosened, he tightens it.  
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to loosen it, due to corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or an abscess, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster, and treat what has come there in ways of healing. 
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reset the plaster and remove it until it is healed.  
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that a fracture of the ribs only occurs in their thickness after the back, and they only bend because they are slippery; 
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one feels it well upon inquiry as it should be.  
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put the break straight as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on a plaster, and remove it with a spatula, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the fracture of the ribs is inward sloping, the patient feels great pain and pressure, as well as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane. 
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And it sweats profusely, and he coughs up a large amount of blood, and this is dangerous illness, and the ancients have put much effort into it. 
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, in order to drive out the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, so that hot abscesses may not come, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if there has come, so he is healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they say that one puts cupping glasses on the place to suck out the pus, and it seems reasonable.  
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Nevertheless, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not draw the superfluities to the place because of the weakness. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say one should cover the place with linen moistened in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to keep the bandage even, then it is cured by the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot suffer because of the bone which points at the cloth, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut on the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put under the instrument to keep the syringe. 
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must cut the bone and drain it slightly, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it heals.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if boils come out, put on cloths moistened in rose oil, and place them on the area. 
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat while the place of that which it belongs to an abscess, and let it lie often on the side where it should be until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a bone fracture occurs at the neck, and sometimes it rains. 
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also in the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take care if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in several positions, and if he moves them and feels well when they are extracted and do not move, know that the junction of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if care is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will heal or not, see if its flesh is softened, and if the accidents are in hands, and on the back there is flatulence and discharge without volition; 
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one turns it on its stomach, if there is discharge without volition.  
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and he wants to get up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal: 
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if one does not labor in its cure. 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this mishap does not befall him, the thing is easier.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you consider if there is a hot abscess, if you put rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is appeased; 
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest. 
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed. 
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bones are broken, it is fitting to cover them over the heart;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with stitches, then treat it with ointment that hardens flesh, until it is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," put your left hand pouch under it and set it equal to the other hand with your power, then apply the plaster and splint on top, if you need them. 
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then remove it, and if there are broken bones, set them, remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.  
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Sometimes it happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it does happen, there would only be a slight reduction in height at the head;
