et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and extending along its length, and sloping downwards, and coming to the patient with pain in the area, and tingling, and swelling where it is broken. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above, as far as you are above the fracture;  
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know which is the fracture and its shape; 
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is only at the head, you put that fracture back together, as long as it is in its natural shape.  
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inwards, then make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that break appears to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have put it back together equally, put plaster on it, then put a splint of wood or horn on top, and immobilize the fracture so that it does not move; 
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply the place below the ribs, as long as the ligature is equal. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a boil comes, do not touch it, until the boil is calmed down, and put what we have said before on it; 
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and remove it as is appropriate, if there is no bad accident; 
et c’est li maniere.	and that is the way. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the shoulder blade and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of two ways: 
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a smooth stick of medium thickness, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two ends with two ties, and hang them up high, and place the patient on a seat;  
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then let the patient's arm be broken on a stick, until it reaches the armpit, and put a bend in the stick, then lean it on some heavy object or have someone hold it down. 
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then place the splints at the break so that they are equal in both hands, as long as the break returns to its proper position. 
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one sets the patient on their back, and ties their hand to their neck, then commands two ministers that one hold what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below at all the ligature, and each extends at his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, extract the ligature below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, you must put one splint below the armpit and the other towards the elbow, below the break. 
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And also if the break is towards the elbow, it is necessary to put a splint lightly, without effort, as long as the break is equal on the place and on the elbow.  
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then set the break equally, as it should be, and remove it, if no abscess comes. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if a boil comes, do not extract it until seven days have passed, and place softened linen soaked in rose oil upon it until the boil is soothed. 
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then extract it, and the way to extract it is that you put a plaster on the breaking point, then bind the arm onto the shoulder joint, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast. 
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And place the cloth, and extract it on the shoulder joint, and on the arm so that the arm is in its proper place, if nothing hinders it, or if no bone is moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone might move, then use splints and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have two finger spaces between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three finger widths on each side. 
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then pull on the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter about fractures, stronger and less distant. 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the seat of the splints and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you set the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, leave it to be tied until the seventh day, as we have said. 
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look at the bandage every three days, so that itching does not occur, or swelling comes to the place, where the nourishments cannot come to the limb because it is too tight. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if none of these accidents come, do not untie it except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back with his hands on his stomach. 
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	And put a cushion of plain wool equally under the shoulder, and look every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or the bandages are loosened. 
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If it is treated by the power of medicine, and given the meat we have mentioned before in part so that the meat is first subtle; 
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And when it begins to regain strength, let it be thick. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be recovered in 40 days altogether;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must untie them and administer baths and ointments for healing the place. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and obstructed, it will remain for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "humerus", one of which is small, and this is the one that enters the shoulder socket.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	And the other is large, and this is the one that is below, towards the little finger. 
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Sometimes only the large humerus breaks, or only the small one, and sometimes both together.  
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When small bones are broken, restoration is easy, and healing. 
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when large bones are broken, healing is difficult, and more grievous than when they are broken together as one. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it is necessary to gently extend it, and set it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is a large bone, it is necessary to bind it tighter; 
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it on a cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed upon himself, and the cushion in front of him higher up so that the patient does not suffer any pain.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the minister's arm below his hand, or at the joint, and another minister above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the sights equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any that is detached so that it holds onto the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before, on bone and sinew.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if there is a break with a wound, I have spoken of it in a separate chapter.
si pren la cure.	If you take the care. 
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of the restoration boils arise, then apply a poultice made of rose oil and white wax, that is neither too hard nor too soft. 
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And bind the poultice on subtly, until the boils are soothed.  
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the wax, and apply a plaster of mill powder with plenty of egg yolks, then place the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be stronger now, and a little wider than the others. 
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	And know that it should have six splints or braces in several positions: 
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	Whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two. 
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	And apply more pressure above the fracture than elsewhere, and every day less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter. 
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	And let the cloths that are upon the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; 
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And let the thread with which it is bound be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And watch over the limb and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is fitting that you wash the limb with hot water, until the itching is appeased; 
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be tightly bound while resting. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again the tightening, and if the ligaments are softened and the bone loosened, and similar things, if so address.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you are careful so that the nourishment cannot reach the limb, because it is too narrow, then you must soften it a little and leave it like that for several days, until the nourishment comes, and then remove it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things which we have said happen to the patient, do not loosen it for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	When you are bandaging, then let him keep his hands at his neck, and let his collars be equal, and let him beware of movement and shaking, and let him sleep on his back; 
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And know that this fracture is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and perhaps in XX days, according to the constitutions and complexions of the humors. 
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and like us we have two fingers which have a bit of splintering, and there is nothing else but weeping many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sit upright and straight in front of him equally; 
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then put his hand on the table extended, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and put them equally the benchmarks, as long as they are well joined; 
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the place; 
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and it is wrapped in a linen cloth. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is at the base around the belly of the palm, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to squeeze it onto his broken palm; 
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then strain it with a long cloth, and let the splint be of hard wood as large as the palm of the hand, and strain it, as it is necessary. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is below, it is fitting that you place a splint above and another below on the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand and bind the ligature between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to any of our bones, it is the one that pushes out, then he must set it equal as it should be. 
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	And he extracts it with the palm, and if you see it put a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and it does not move. 
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the fracture is in other bones, such as the index finger or one of the others, then he sets it equal and binds it with the healthy bone that is next to it. 
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	Or you bind them all together, as much as they are worth, or you put them on a splint, such as a pouch.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And take care in the restoration and arrangement of hot abscesses, and cure those who come to you, as I have said.  
de la cuixe brisie	Of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns forward and backward; 
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And the restoration is one ties above the fracture, and another below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his tie to his own part equally; 
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is near the bone. 
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, one of the bandages should be towards the hip, and the other bandages below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then let the ties be below the knee, and let the extension be downward; 
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then place the splints against the bone equal to his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then put on the plaster, and the tie, if abscesses do not appear. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside, then return to your work and your care;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The binding is done in a partial manner. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap it on the fracture with a bandage doubled two or three times, and leave the excess, then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the head of the thread above; 
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn the bandage on the leg and thigh, then put splints on the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; 
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloths to make the constriction even, then begin to tie three or four turns on the fracture; 
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and when you go further up the fracture, tighten it less; 
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two ends of the thread that you have put between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints that are above it, then go back down to the head of the thread until you reach below the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, then so that there comes neither an abscess nor swelling nor any other such thing. 
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens and it loosens, and corrects what comes, as we have said many times;  
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, it must be removed if possible; 
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if it is not possible, it is necessary to split the area and draw out force; 
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And when the thigh is broken in this way, one puts splints on it as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	in all ways, the patient does not sound a bell when restoration is done like this. 
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee hollow
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that on the street of the knee there is often no fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is but a crack or a hole, and occurs in every wound, and in every wound, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And restoration is done when one puts together what is broken with its due parts, as long as it can be assembled and moved. 
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then apply a plaster, and put a round splint if needed, and remove it as appropriate. Then observe all the arrangements that we have mentioned for other fractures, such as abscess cautery and other similar things. 
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Apply to each injury what is appropriate until it is healed.  
de la brisure de la jambe	of a leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called "musculus" and the other is called "fibula". 
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And all other fractures occur as they do in the arm, and for this reason, restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the operations are the same. And if both bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bones are broken, turn them forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, then there is great pain, and it is clearly seen. 
et torne desoz.	and turns downward.  
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then apply extension, and set it equal, and tie the splints evenly; 
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but nevertheless, if the break is severe, and there are several pieces, the extension should be less and lighter; 
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and the alignment according to your skill. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed all your work, take two bandages of unbleached linen that can cover the leg on one side and the other, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee down; 
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap them around twice above and below, and tie them in the middle as well, and at this binding the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; 
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one should administer herbs of the length of the leg, and if it is wood, and he puts it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly do this in the fracture where there is a wound 
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, to see if there is a hot abscess or another incident; 
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the healer so much as he is healthy. 
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	There is no fracture at the ankle, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and there are two possibilities, and there are no other conditions except in several positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it happens that a bone in the foot is broken, and you see these bones rise against each other, put the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot now on his, where the bones are raised, then press it so much that they return to their places; 
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then put the plaster and bandages on top, and put under the belly of the foot a small board with two inches thick, then straighten the foot carefully, and after you have wrapped cloths around it, and other things that you need. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the two bones are broken, then restore them, as we have said for the bones of the hand. 
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and make it a little wider, then put the footboard under that splint as I have said, and bind it tightly. 
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then put a splint on each bone according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the splint under the foot. 
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And let it be resting on the top of the splint above the belly of the foot so that it holds it well.  
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, as we have already discussed. 
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And treat each injury according to its needs.  
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone by the dagger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of a woman by nature is broken, make her sit enlarged, then incline her to the back part, and let her be held from behind. 
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	Then fill the hollow of the patient's nature with cotton, and put in it as large as I stand. 
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then raise the woman, and lift her back little by little, and then the cotton jumps, as far as it comes to the entrance of the nature, and return the bone with the stick. 
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and thus do for seven days or so.  
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	Then the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of a lamb, and tie to the opening a cane, and insert the whole bladder into the nature.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow into the cane, so that the bladder swells inside. 
la nature si revenra li brisure;	nature will heal the fracture; 
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it should be filled with cotton, and left like that for several days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of a man or woman's shoulder is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; 
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these nearby fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and use, and understand my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture indicates in several positions the right way of restoration: 
enten le donques.	understand then. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	When the penis is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert the penis into it;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be cleansed now, so that the cleansings which we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, and you have no other remedy, then start again to restore the fracture in the same hour or day, so that abscesses do not form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess comes there, leave the restoration until a new day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you will cause bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the chest uncovered, it is fitting that you set it straight lightly with your hands, with little extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension does not appear to you to put it evenly with your hands, then use this instrument made of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; 
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and therefore it is necessary for the doctor to grasp three or four, according to what he needs in each treatment of a fracture 
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let it be round and one thick piece so that it does not fold under pressure on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick from the middle forward, like this: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called a "splint", because it is necessary that the curved head be placed on the top of the visible bone; 
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and the end at one time, so that it returns to its place, and is equal on both sides.  
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot properly grasp the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, if the edge of a suitable instrument for this, either an incision knife or saw, is at your disposal;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove what remains in the bone of sharpness and small splinters. 
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is put back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Do as much as you can so that it is in its place, then moisten a cloth with black balsamic vinegar, and do this properly if it is summer. 
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	And do not put any wax or anything else on the wound that has oil, lest it cause decay and corruption. 
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	Then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and put a covering all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not strained with the break.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	And many times this has been done foolishly, and has brought death or corrosion upon the patient sometimes. 
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And let the binding be looser and softer than for other fractures.  
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents might come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not right to put on splints.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	But wrap around it, instead of bandages, hard cloths, and bind them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the gut in the wound begins to move, remove what you have put on it with all wine, and apply healing ointment, such as Tetrafarmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be aligned in such a way that the bone runs down slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day it passes and it cannot be soldered but continually bows back, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must want the wound with a tent, and remove all these detached pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or some other manner of corruption, it is fitting that you cure it according to what he says in his chapter before this one.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and appears on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not pull it at all, for many times death comes, but leave it until it rots.  
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	It may fall off by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if you cannot, leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of burns that come from solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	It often happens after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a sorry thing to see the shape of the limb.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	And perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.  
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Therefore be careful if it is fresh to us: 
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	If he administers astringent medicines, such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others, so that you take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with the white of an egg or with oil; 
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	And put them on the wound in bandages, and bind it well, and do not unbind it in any way.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	And then loosen it, and begin another one, until the swelling is removed; 
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	Or you bind on a well-made piece of linen;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	For the property of linen is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; 
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	And if the swelling has already become hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, apply a cup over it, and make the excess appear; 
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Where you shave it with any razor, until it is removed, and heal it until it is cured. 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the bone fracture is restored and the limbs remain weak and delicate afterwards, it happens for many reasons. 
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	One reason is because it was tied too tightly and was not bound as it should have been.  
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	Or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not reach the limb. 
ou por multitude d’arosement;	Or because of a great deal of agitation.
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	Or for too much movement at the wrong time.
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	Or because he has little blood in his body and is therefore weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and soften his body, so that his blood is multiplied within him. 
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and he administers a bath, and gives him joy and relief; 
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then he puts pitch on the limb, so that the pitch draws out great numbness, and he often warms it with hot water, until the numbness goes away from the limb; 
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and it returns to its natural shape. 
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a crooked limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: 
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, and many a fool has done this in our land; 
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and it leads to great evils, and by chance death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	however, if the nodules and the tortures are fresh, it is necessary that they be warmed with hot water, or soft herbs be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; 
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and apply a softening plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with gelatin fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; 
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take fatty figs, and crush them with bran, and similar medicines that reduce swelling. 
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation removed by continuous and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be administered to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the crookedness is old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with an iron, then carefully cut to the bone with a fine chisel. 
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and apply caution and diligence in the treatment. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, it must now be brought back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if you delay, the flesh will swell, and it may be put back in its place with difficulty; 
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	therefore it is not right to move it while it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	Many times it brings forth spasm and other pains; 
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	In any case, when this happens, if you make the patient well, then leave him alone until the abscesses are appeased; 
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it lightly, and treat each member as it comes into its place.  
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It sometimes happens that both jaws are dislocated, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: 
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	where they are at one time removed from their places, and softened a little bit;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated and hang toward the chin, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with speech.  
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through several manipulations.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it quickly and do not delay; 
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a manner that the assistants hold the head of the patient, and put the point of a mirror into the root of the jaw dislocation in the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; 
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other hand should be free, to put it equal; 
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.  
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let him look at the same spot until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the reduction is difficult, even if both jaws are together, apply hot water and oil until they soften slightly;  
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not delay the reduction as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reduced evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, put soft cloths dipped in cerate made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages; 
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient lie on his back, and his shoulders be placed between two cushions, so that he does not move either to the right or to the left, nor does he try to raise himself, but takes light food, as long as the pains are removed, and the jaws are bound; 
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then let him eat what he wants lightly, and do not work at opening his mouth to eat or drink, as long as the jaw is well bound and clean. 
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not converted to their places, fever and accustomed colds will come, and possibly loosening of the belly, and possibly vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is lost; 
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times they died in nine days. 
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The cautery cannot dislocate from within the continuation of the leg and foot, and it is dislocated sometimes by force, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and extends his arms; 
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the place with your palm, and it will return;  
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	Then put on the plaster and bandage it, and remove it; 
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	And the head which is towards the knife cannot dislocate; 
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	If it does, and if it dislocates sometimes, reset it in its place, as we have said; 
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then put on the plaster and bandage it, and remove it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; 
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in the same way, reset the head of the shoulder when it is dislocated from its place.  
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is only dislocated according to three manners: 
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	Of which one is when it dislocates at the part of the armpit below;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	And the second is at the part of the breast; 
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	And by chance it dislocates at the part above, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and do not dislocate it behind for the shoulder, and do not dislocate it inwards for the nerves; 
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and many times dislocate it downwards towards the armpit, especially for those who have a short neck, for this salt must be forced quickly; 
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	for those who have enough neck, the salt is taken with difficulty, and put back in with difficulty.  
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it sometimes happens that some men experience a bruise or fracture, and their shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of it.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore it behoves you to test it until you are certain of it;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment. 
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that the dislocation occurs when it falls towards the armpit and puts a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear diversity between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the armpit at the buttock the head of the shoulder, as if it were a bone. 
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot return his hand to its place, nor move it in any way; 
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated at the top, unless it is hidden, for you will find it manifestly by touch; 
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation is not very difficult to reset, when it is new, or if the child's arm is ill. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the manner is that the attendant lifts the patient's hand upwards, then puts your fingers under the armpit, and lifts the joint forcefully upwards to its place; 
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the attendant lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then puts it underneath;  
si venra hastanment.	it will come quickly. 
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said within three days, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; 
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And give him a softening and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of marshmallow and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be applied. 
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then have the patient lie on his back, and put under the armpit a cloth of wool neither too soft nor too hard. Then place the mires (a kind of bandage) with the patient's heel on the cloth, and gently lift the head of the shoulder, and pull the patient’s hand; 
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another assistant should hold the patient’s head so that it does not move down.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	This shoulder will now return to its place, and if you see that the resetting according to this manner 
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and have a man larger than the patient present.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And he should stand straight towards the side, and put his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit upwards so that the patient hangs by the arm.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And another minister will pull the patient's hand down towards their belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can hold something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And one can reset it in another way: 
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and this is done by sticking a long iron rod into the ground, whose head should be as round as a pestle, and not too thick nor too thin;  
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it should be placed under the patient, but with soft cloths underneath, and the patient should lie lengthwise along the wood; 
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then their hand should be extended downwards on the other side, and the joint will quickly return to its place; 
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return because of all these things that we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take an iron rod two arm lengths long and four inches wide, which has a round head to easily enter underneath the armpit, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then lay upon the head of the wound cloths underneath so that the wound does not bleed on the patient, then put it under the armpit of the patient. 
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	Extend some arm upon the wood of length, and tie the shoulder upon the wood, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm upon the shoulder-blade of a ladder of width, and let the hand be extended downwards, and let the body hang down on the other side: 
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint will return to its place while being held. 
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, no matter how, you must put a sphere of equal wool under the shoulder, then apply plaster mixed with powdered mill flour, incense and egg yolk, over the entire shoulder and around it. Then tighten it under the shoulder carefully and turn the bandage on top of the plaster, embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is fitting that he rests a bit, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; 
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then rest more afterwards for five or seven days, and move it;  
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture or some other cause, you must administer cauteries at three points, as described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it loosens after VII days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise its arm up, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened. 
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And know that the joint was never fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is towards the back, and the breasts, or buttocks, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the hands, and administered in another place.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cure it as long as it is healthy. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness in the limb, and slow movement, then let the patient bathe many times, until the stiffness is relieved and it returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of dislocation, what is done.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated at points, and at points it returns.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	And if it is dislocated from all sides, and the same in front and behind, and the dislocation is not answered, for one sees it well and feels it well.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and it dislocates according to each shape. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick knife with the healthy one, if you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is lifted, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you must reset it so that abscesses do not come, for if abscesses were to come, it would be harmful to reset. 
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	And by chance it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the back; 
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations and causes greater pain, and by chance death may come. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration, when it is such that you can reset it, is done by extending your hand with both hands.  
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And his arms should be spread, and both hands should look according to the turn of the wound, above and below, and push the joint into its socket, or at the base of his palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is forward, it returns when he doubles his hand onto his hand, and touches the root of the palm or the costal which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply strong extension; 
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and when the minister extends the arm, and holds it so that it does not move during the extension. 
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm from each side, once you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it;  
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the minister joins the joint with his hand, if oil is needed to soften the joint, then push the joint into place, until it returns. 
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, put dry plaster with egg yolk on top and bind it firmly, then rest the arm against the patient's neck and leave it for several days, then unbind it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it.  
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint is not set well, start the plaster and bandage again, and leave it like this for several days until it is firmly in place. 
puis le deslie.	Then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved. 
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Or put a fatty sheep's wool on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then bone it, and make it enter the bath. 
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	And when he sweats, if he rubs the joint moderately, then put the wool back on and then enter the bath.  
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this two or three times until he is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see it, put cow dung moistened with heated butter on it, and bind it up. 
si revenra a sa disposition.	It will return to its position. 
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and its return is easier than that of other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to quickly return it to its place, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the flesh does not swell or become hot with an abscess. 
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the return is done so that you put the ailing hand on a table and extend the fingers of the hand; then look at it and align it evenly, so that it puts its palm on the appearance of the joint and pushes it until it returns.  
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Nevertheless, it is necessary that you look to see if it is well in place; 
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the patient's back of his hand on a table for stretching and pulling. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the doctor put his hand on that part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it is good. 
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, apply soothing poultices for abscesses and leave it thus without restarting. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after a few days, the joint will remain crooked; 
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and it does not harm the patient further than that his hand is weakened and he cannot grasp anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; 
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other remedy than to burn it with a cautery in this case, and perhaps nothing else will do.  
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then unbind it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some pain, then apply hot water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulders of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the two bones of the hand are dislocated in each direction, sometimes at the back of the palm or on the belly; 
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then hold the pain, and push the dislocation towards your pouches as much as it returns, then support the head of the joint, and bend it towards the part where it is separated; 
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, and then set it equal that day;  
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and bind it at night as we have said, and unbind it during the day, and make it move, and bind it at night; 
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is tight, and also do this if it is dislocated in the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed. 
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do the same when it is dislocated elsewhere.  
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Concerning the dislocation of the shoulder blade from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that movements jump strong without will, and he cannot hold them, and many times some limb is softened, whether it be both thighs or both arms or one. 
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the shinbone is broken into four parts; 
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which breaks in the back is called "gilbositez" 
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The treatment is that you will consider if the gilbositez came from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is neither cure nor healing at all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient manners of treatment are said in great words, where there is not much profit in all;  
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that for the gilbositez which comes at the front of the foot, there is neither remedy nor healing;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes straight on both sides, and one cannot cure except that which properly comes to the back, as I say. 
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And it is necessary that the patient be laid flat on his face in an even place, and have a support underneath him so he does not blanch. 
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then place one coal at the head in earth form, and the other at his feet, and tie a strap under the patient's buttocks, and another at his thighs, and at his shins, and at his ankles. 
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	And two assistants should hold the straps, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two coals. 
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And they should be well secured, the coals as we have said, and the healer should place his palms on the spine, in a straight line, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this treatment, then take a board three arm's lengths long, and place it under the wall, and have the patient lie on his side, and push his head from the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board on the spine. 
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put your feet on the other end of the table, and press hard, until it returns to its place; 
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see it, do it with the screw that turns the hand. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And place two embers at the head of the patient's arm, and two others towards the feet, and between each ember, above and below, a palm's breadth in length.
