et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	And make a hole in each ember where the screw runs, and set the embers firmly in the ground so they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And between each two embers place a turning ember, with which the limbs turn, and place in the two turning embers two small embers a palm's length long to turn the screw.  
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then tie the cord which is among the splints to the screw towards the head, and the other cord to the screw towards the feet, and each of the assistants turns his screw on the whole cord, and the master puts the spine straight as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are equal, put a drying plaster on them with plenty of egg, and then bandages, and then the stele of a tablet three fingers long, which covers the place of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the vertebra, then tie it with a linen cloth, as we have said, and use the patient with subtle nourishment until he is healed. 
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if anything comes at the end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the stele that we have said before. 
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And sometimes one administers a plum stone, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back vertebra of the back, and one thinks that it is a dislocation.  
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	And it is the bone that appears, for which one should not have presumption. 
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	By chance death might come. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come out of place by dislocations, not in the same way as the other joints. 
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	And the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts:  
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inward and outward, and in front and behind. 
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	And more inward than others, and rarely dislocated in front and behind.  
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the recognition of this inward dislocation is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee towards the fire. 
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And there is a swelling below like a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there.   
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who is coming to death is if this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of one who has it beforehand, if they are well their leg according to its completion. 
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Nevertheless, do not bend the knee twice without pain, and if one wants to make it go, it cannot beforehand, and it retains its urine, and swells the ankle, and when it goes, it passes on the heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of someone who has it behind are that he cannot straighten his knee or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the angle is softened, and the head of the thigh is at a place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The reduction of this kind of dislocation is such that you consider if the dislocation is old, and it stays according to its disposition, there is no cure. 
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it is not fitting for him to have presumption.  
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in that one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of four manners of dislocation, hasten yourself so that you return the joint, and extend it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left. 
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	perhaps it will return, and needs no other remedy.  
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare a strong assistant, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or with a bandage tied above the knee; 
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	And another assistant extends his hand on top in such a way that he puts his hands under his armpits, then he binds it tightly with a rope above the thigh; 
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another holds the head of the rope; 
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this does not work, then it is necessary to treat it in a similar manner. 
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the thigh, it is necessary that you lay the patient on his healthy side, then put the bandage at the root of the thigh, and the place which is below the groin, then stretch the bandage upwards towards the groin, and towards the knee-cap; 
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then take another minister and have him embrace the thick part of the sick person's thigh with his arms, and extend it towards the fire. 
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	It will now return to its place. 
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	And this method of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have said, then it is fitting that you bind the two feet of the sick person together with a strong band, tightly above the two heels and above the two knees, and let the sick leg be extended two fists more than the others; 
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then it is hung on the top of a pole, and is above the ground by two arm's lengths.
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then command one minister to embrace the top of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the sick person, who embraces firmly the thigh, for the joint now returns quickly.  
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is outward, if the patient lies down as we have said for one with gout, and tighten the bandage on the affected leg properly, and on the foot also. 
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then place two pieces of burning wood, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert one piece of burning wood between the patient's thighs in the shape. 
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And put cloths soaked in water around it so that they do not burn the patient, then extend each of his limbs towards him and have him place his hand on the dislocation.  
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on a table, and press as we said in the guild.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is forward, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly and according as I have said. 
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And put his hand on the pain of being on the affected angle and then press with the other hand, and extend it down towards the knee.  
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is not fitting to stretch the patient out, nor raise him up, but he should be as when his hip was dislocated in the shoulder, as we have said about childbirth on both hips. 
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And he should be on his face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table; 
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be in place when the patient stretches his legs, and they will be equal;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the thighs, and apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; 
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rest for three or four days, then unbind it, and apply plaster on top;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are equal, bind it as before, and leave it for three days; 
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Then untie it, and make it move smoothly, until the limb is comfortable. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated according to three manners: 
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	That is to say, inwards and outwards, and backwards; 
et ne desalue point devant.	and it does not dislocate forwards. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not bend at his thigh, know that it is dislocated; 
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all such is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; 
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee joint; 
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another assistant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he bends his leg at his thigh easily; 
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put the plaster on it, and let the leg air dry at the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three days or four, then unbind it. 
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the patient should not be troubled to go until the limb is comfortable. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not set, then administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes strained, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	The signs are that the ankle is swollen and tense before the part where it is dislocated:  
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the reduction is slight, and one must extend the finger slightly towards their hand when it is only loosened. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, it is fitting that you make the patient sit upright and hold them firmly by the leg above the ankle. 
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upwards, and push the foot beautifully upward. 
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; 
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns, it is good; 
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, start the work again, for it will return; 
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return this way, have the patient lie on his back on the ground, and insert a firm stick into the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around so that he does not bruise the patient;  
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then have one assistant hold the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot with his hands or a strap which he ties around the ankle; 
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then have each assistant extend equally, and let the stick be now between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when he is being extended;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then place the assistant's hands equally on the dislocation, and have another assistant hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is at the point, put the plaster and bandages on top, and bind them firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are on the ankle behind, so that the bandages are not too tight. 
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, bind them again. 
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days. 
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if he goes before that time, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is necessary that you soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they are nicely extended without effort, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any of the joints of the back of the foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or table straight, and put your foot on what appears of those joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns. 
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is equal and there appears nothing, then place under the sole of the foot a table with two legs, then bind it tightly and leave it for three days, then unbind it. 
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it rest until it is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and of dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation and one wants to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:  
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow, do not dare; 
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And at the beginning use soothing things to draw out the abscess heat, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health; 
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, then reset the limb in its place, so that the abscess pus may come out. 
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things to the hot abscess, and heal the wound as it should be, with drying ointments; 
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if the dislocation is with a fracture, and small bones are broken off, let the surgeon do what we have said in simple diseases; 
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and beware of entering the way of fear, as I have said, for this is worth more according to your creator, and for the safety of your soul and body.
